# ENFORCEMENT BOARD DIGEST  research=20/20  adversarial=17/20

=================== RESEARCH ===================

### settings.json schema & permission precedence
The official Claude Code settings.json schema (schemastore.org + code.claude.com/docs) exposes a 5-layer hierarchy (managed > CLI args > local > project > user) where permission rules MERGE across layers rather than override, deny beats allow at every layer, and a handful of keys are managed-only. For Ultron/Kenning on Windows 11 the critical insight is: (1) deny rules from ANY scope block regardless of allow rules at any other scope; (2) disableBypassPermissionsMode and allowManagedPermissionRulesOnly live inside the permissions object and are read from any scope but are most authoritative in managed settings; (3) hooks use exit-code-2 for blocking, exit-0+JSON for allow/deny/ask/defer decisions; (4) the Stop-hook deadlock trap requires checking stop_hook_active; (5) on Windows, Node.js is always present and preferred over bash+jq for hook scripts; (6) the deny-not-enforced bug (issue #6699) was observed at v1.0.93 and is now closed, but a belt-and-suspenders PreToolUse hook is warranted for any path you care deeply about; (7) the official settings-strict.json example shows disableBypassPermissionsMode nested inside permissions, and WebSearch/WebFetch in the deny array - directly applicable to the kit.
- [DENY|both|risk:low|high] Permission rules MERGE (union) across all five settings layers - they do NOT override. A deny rule in ANY layer (managed/local/project/user) blocks the tool regardless of allow rules elsewhere. The precedence order within evaluation is: deny → ask → allow, first-match wins, and rule specificity does NOT change order. A broad Bash(aws *) deny blocks Bash(aws s3 ls) allow unconditionally. => Place your hardest deny rules (canon-file protection, anticheat import-firewall, secrets) in .claude/settings.json (project scope) so they merge with any user-level rules rather than relying on user scope alone. Example snippet for Ultron: { "permissions": { "deny": ["Read(**/.env)", "Read(**/secrets/**)", "Bash(pip install *)", "Bash(pip3 install *)"] } }. Do NOT try to add a narrower allow to carve out exceptions from a deny - it will be silently ignored.
- [DENY|both|risk:low|high] disableBypassPermissionsMode and disableAutoMode sit INSIDE the permissions object (not at top-level settings), accept the string value "disable", and work from any settings scope - not managed-only. bypassPermissions mode still prompts for rm -rf / and rm -rf ~ as a circuit breaker. Explicit ask rules in settings still force a prompt even in bypassPermissions. On Windows/Linux, Claude Code refuses to start in bypassPermissions when running as root/sudo. => Add both keys to the project .claude/settings.json for Ultron and to the kit's template. This prevents any session from silently entering full-bypass mode via --dangerously-skip-permissions without a managed policy. For the kit (project scope): set disableBypassPermissionsMode to "disable". For Ultron's local dev runs where you may need bypass for scripted testing, override only in .claude/settings.local.json (gitignored). Note: disableAutoMode should also be "disable" for Ultron since the auto-mode classifier drops broad Bash(*) allow rules on entry.
- [CONFIG|both|risk:none|high] defaultMode is a key inside the permissions object (not top-level). Valid values (from schemastore.org JSON schema): acceptEdits, bypassPermissions, default, delegate, dontAsk, plan, auto. Setting defaultMode: "auto" in .claude/settings.json or settings.local.json is SILENTLY IGNORED since Claude Code v2.1.142 - it must be in ~/.claude/settings.json (user scope) or managed settings to take effect. dontAsk mode auto-denies every tool call that would otherwise prompt, making it suitable for CI but not for interactive sessions. => For Ultron: set defaultMode: "default" in .claude/settings.json to anchor the session in safe-prompt mode. Never set "auto" or "bypassPermissions" in project settings - they are silently ignored or blocked respectively. For the kit: set defaultMode: "default" in the project settings template. For CI/headless runs, use the --permission-mode dontAsk flag at invocation rather than baking it into shared settings.
- [CONFIG|ultron|risk:none|high] additionalDirectories is an array inside the permissions object. It grants file read/edit access to extra paths under the same permission rules as the working directory. CRITICALLY: when set via settings.json (as opposed to --add-dir CLI flag or /add-dir command), it grants file access ONLY - it does NOT load .claude/ config, agents, skills, or hooks from those directories. Only --add-dir/add-dir command exceptions load config from additional dirs. => For Ultron, use additionalDirectories to grant access to E:\UltronModels\ and E:\ultron_resources\ without giving those paths config discovery authority. Do NOT rely on additionalDirectories for loading subagents or hooks from secondary worktrees - use --add-dir at invocation instead. Windows paths normalize to POSIX before matching, so use //e/UltronModels/** in deny/allow rules for drive-specific patterns.
- [CONFIG|both|risk:none|high] allowManagedPermissionRulesOnly and allowManagedHooksOnly are managed-only keys (reading them from user/project/local settings has NO effect). When true, all user and project allow/ask/deny permission rules are completely ignored - only managed-tier rules apply. The official settings-strict.json example places these at the TOP LEVEL of the JSON (not inside permissions), alongside the permissions object. => For a personal/solo project like Ultron (no MDM/managed deployment), these keys provide zero benefit in .claude/settings.json since they require the managed layer. Do NOT add them to project settings expecting them to work - they will be silently ignored. If the user ever deploys via MDM or C:\Program Files\ClaudeCode\managed-settings.json, that is where to place these. For the kit: document that these are managed-only and provide a managed-settings template separately from the project settings template.
- [DENY|ultron|risk:med|high] Bare tool-name deny rules (e.g., "Bash" or "WebSearch" without parentheses) REMOVE the tool from Claude's context entirely - Claude never sees or attempts to use it. A scoped deny like "Bash(rm *)" leaves the tool available but blocks matching calls when Claude attempts them. A deny rule whose tool name matches no known tool at startup emits a startup WARNING to catch typos. Wildcard deny rules like "mcp__*" deny ALL MCP tools from ALL servers. => For Ultron's anticheat context: use bare "WebSearch" and "WebFetch" denies if you want those tools completely invisible to Claude (prevents prompt injection from web content). For MCP servers you want to block entirely, use "mcp__servername" bare or "mcp__servername__*" wildcard. For the canon-file protection use scoped denies: "Edit(/docs/canon/**)" and "Edit(/.claude/settings.json)" - these leave the tools available but block specific paths. Note: these scoped denies for protected paths are in ADDITION to PreToolUse hooks (defense-in-depth).
- [HOOK|ultron|risk:low|high] Hook decisions do NOT bypass permission rules. A PreToolUse hook returning permissionDecision: "allow" does NOT override a deny rule in settings - the deny rule still fires. Conversely, a PreToolUse hook exiting with code 2 (block) takes precedence over allow rules. This asymmetry means hooks and permission rules are additive security layers: hooks can only ADD restrictions or give advisory allow signals, never remove deny-rule enforcement. The hookSpecificOutput.permissionDecision field lives inside a nested object: { hookSpecificOutput: { hookEventName: "PreToolUse", permissionDecision: "deny", permissionDecisionReason: "..." } }. => Layer hooks ON TOP of deny rules, never as a replacement. For Ultron's anticheat import-firewall: keep the deny rules for pip/curl/wget in settings.json AND add a PreToolUse hook that scans Bash commands for blocked import patterns - the hook catches edge cases (compound commands, env wrappers) while the deny rule is the hard gate. For the Stop hook backing CI gates: always check stop_hook_active in the input JSON and exit 0 immediately when true to prevent self-deadlock loops.
- [HOOK|both|risk:high|high] Stop-hook self-deadlock is a documented hard trap: a Stop hook that always blocks (exit 2 or decision:block) loops forever because Claude immediately re-enters a Stop → block → re-run cycle. The hook input JSON includes a stop_hook_active boolean field that is true when a Stop hook is actively running. A Stop hook MUST check this field and exit 0 when true. Scope Stop hooks to changed files in the current turn and back them with CI to avoid over-blocking. => For Ultron's pre-push hygiene Stop hook: read stdin JSON, check stop_hook_active field, exit 0 immediately if true. Only run the hygiene checks (ruff/mypy/test-map) when stop_hook_active is false. Never put an unconditional exit-2 in a Stop hook. Use asyncRewake: true for CI-style checks that should wake Claude on failure without blocking the stop entirely.
- [DENY|kit|risk:high|high] The official settings-strict.json example (anthropics/claude-code repo) places disableBypassPermissionsMode: "disable" INSIDE the permissions object, and places allowManagedPermissionRulesOnly and allowManagedHooksOnly at the TOP LEVEL (sibling of permissions). It also includes a sandbox object with network restrictions and disables WebSearch/WebFetch via deny. The WebSearch/WebFetch deny in settings-strict.json WILL block deep research, WebFetch, and all autonomous web access - this is a critical blocker risk for the kit's deep-research workflows. => For the Kit: do NOT copy settings-strict.json verbatim - it denies WebSearch and WebFetch which are essential for deep-research, WebFetch, and multi-agent workflows. Instead use a settings-moderate.json approach: keep disableBypassPermissionsMode:"disable" and the sandbox restrictions, but allow WebSearch/WebFetch or scope WebFetch to allowed domains. For Ultron specifically: deny WebSearch and WebFetch entirely (anticheat risk - Claude should never make network calls while Valorant+Vanguard are running) but this is Ultron-specific, not kit-wide.
PITFALLS: Deny rules and allow rules are UNIONS across all scopes - a user-level allow CANNOT override a project-level deny. This is often misunderstood as 'higher priority overrides lower'. The actual semantics are: collect all deny rules from all scopes, collect all allow rules from all scopes, evaluate deny first. A project deny beats a user allow. | A deny rule WITHOUT parentheses (bare tool name like 'Bash') removes the tool from Claude's context entirely and generates no error message - Claude simply does not see the tool. A scoped deny like 'Bash(rm *)' leaves the tool visible but blocks matching calls. The distinction matters: bare deny prevents even reading the tool description; scoped deny allows the tool but gates specific patterns. | allowManagedPermissionRulesOnly and allowManagedHooksOnly placed in .claude/settings.json (project scope) are silently ignored - they only work in the managed layer. There is NO warning logged when they appear in non-managed files. | defaultMode: "auto" in .claude/settings.json or .claude/settings.local.json is silently ignored since v2.1.142. This is a documented intentional change to prevent repos from granting themselves auto mode. Moving it to ~/.claude/settings.json is the fix. | The deny-rules-not-enforced bug (GitHub issue #6699) was reported at v1.0.93 and closed without a documented fix version in the issue thread. The current docs describe deny enforcement as working correctly. Always layer a PreToolUse hook as belt-and-suspenders for critical deny rules on sensitive paths. | Compound Bash commands: a rule like 'Bash(npm test *)' does NOT cover 'npm test && rm -rf .' - Claude Code parses compound commands and checks each subcommand independently. A deny on 'Bash(rm *)' will still fire for the rm subcommand. This is protective behavior, but means allow rules for compound commands must cover each part. | Read and Edit deny rules apply to Claude's built-in file tools and recognized Bash commands (cat, head, tail, sed) but NOT to arbitrary subprocesses that open files themselves (e.g., a Python script that does open('.env')). For OS-level enforcement, the sandbox.filesystem option is needed. | On Windows, Read/Edit path rules normalize C:\Users\alice to /c/Users/alice before matching. Use //c/**/.env to match .env files on the C: drive. Cross-drive patterns require separate rules per drive letter or use //**/.env for all drives. | The Stop hook stop_hook_active deadlock is NOT theoretical - any Stop hook that unconditionally exits 2 will loop forever. This is the most dangerous misconfiguration possible in the hooks system. Always gate on stop_hook_active. | Hook permissionDecision: "allow" does NOT bypass deny rules in settings. The deny-first evaluation happens AFTER the hook allow signal. A hook can only add the allow signal; it cannot remove a deny rule's effect. This asymmetry protects against hook compromise but surprises developers who expect hooks to be the final authority. | disableBypassPermissionsMode works from any scope, but is 'most useful in managed settings where they cannot be overridden' per the official docs. In project settings, a user could edit .claude/settings.json to remove it. For hard enforcement, it must be in the managed layer (C:\Program Files\ClaudeCode\managed-settings.json on Windows). | The strictKnownMarketplaces: [] (empty array) in settings-strict.json blocks ALL plugin marketplaces including the Anthropic default. For the kit this would block skill installation. Use strictKnownMarketplaces only if you have a curated internal marketplace or want to completely lock out plugin installs. | The PowerShell rule syntax is separate from Bash - a 'Bash(rm *)' deny does NOT cover PowerShell Remove-Item calls. On Windows (Ultron), add parallel 'PowerShell(Remove-Item *)' deny rules. Common aliases are canonicalized (gci, ls, dir all match Get-ChildItem) but only within the PowerShell rule space.
OPENQ: The deny-not-enforced bug (#6699, v1.0.93) was closed without a documented fix version. What is the minimum version where deny rules are reliably enforced? Should the project's requiredMinimumVersion be set to ensure a fixed build? | Does setting disableBypassPermissionsMode: "disable" in .claude/settings.json (project scope) actually prevent a user from passing --dangerously-skip-permissions at the CLI, or can the CLI flag override project-scoped settings? The docs say 'A deny rule cannot be overridden by --allowedTools' but are unclear whether disableBypassPermissionsMode in project scope truly blocks the CLI flag. | The permissions object schema (from schemastore.org) lists 'delegate' as a valid defaultMode value. This mode is not documented on the permission-modes page. What does delegate mode do? | For Ultron's anticheat context: does the sandbox.network configuration (allowedDomains, deniedDomains) in .claude/settings.json apply to all tool calls including MCP server network requests, or only to Bash commands? The docs say sandboxing 'applies only to Bash commands and their child processes'. | Can a PreToolUse hook's permissionDecision: "allow" signal cause the tool to proceed even when the permission mode is dontAsk and there is no explicit allow rule? Or does dontAsk mode's auto-deny still win? | The docs mention that 'Hook decisions do not bypass permission rules' - does this mean a hook with permissionDecision: "deny" is additive (can add blocks beyond settings denies) but cannot remove blocks? Confirmed for allow; need to verify deny hooks vs. allow settings rules. | For the kit's deep-research workflows: if WebFetch is in the allow list but a managed policy sets allowManagedPermissionRulesOnly: true with no WebFetch allow in managed settings, does deep-research break silently or with an error? Managed-layer exclusive control with missing allows would effectively block kit workflows. | The asyncRewake: true hook option wakes Claude on exit-code-2 failure. Does this work for SubagentStop events too, or only for top-level Stop events? Multi-agent workflows depend on subagent stop hooks for CI gate signaling. | Windows registry-based managed settings (HKLM\SOFTWARE\Policies\ClaudeCode) vs file-based (C:\Program Files\ClaudeCode\managed-settings.json): which takes precedence when both are present? The docs list both as 'managed layer' but do not specify inter-managed priority.

### hook-event-catalog-and-zero-blocking-value
Claude Code exposes 30 hook events across 8 lifecycle phases. Of these, 14 can block (via exit 2 or decision:block JSON), while the remaining 16 are advisory-only (exit code ignored or stderr shown but execution continues). For an enforcement bundle targeting maximum teeth at zero friction, the highest-value zero-blocking-risk hooks are: SessionStart (inject CONSTRAINTS/reground context via additionalContext), UserPromptSubmit (advisory additionalContext injection without the decision:block path), PostToolUse (advisory additionalContext + updatedToolOutput redaction — cannot undo execution), PostCompact (re-inject grounding context after compaction), SubagentStop (audit/logging, stop_hook_active field enables safe gate implementation), and WorktreeCreate (replaces git behavior, must create worktree itself and print path). The PreCompact hook adds value as a snapshot trigger with zero blocking risk if you omit decision:block. The critical self-deadlock trap for Stop hooks is handled by checking stop_hook_active (boolean in JSON input) before returning decision:block. Windows-correct hook syntax requires shell:powershell in the hook config or a Node.js command hook since bash+jq is not guaranteed on Windows 11.
- [ADVISORY|both|risk:none|high] 30 hook events exist across 8 lifecycle phases as of mid-2026. Exactly 14 support blocking (exit 2 or top-level decision:block): PreToolUse, PermissionRequest, UserPromptSubmit, UserPromptExpansion, PostToolBatch, Stop, SubagentStop, TeammateIdle, TaskCreated, TaskCompleted, ConfigChange, PreCompact, Elicitation, ElicitationResult. The remaining 16 are advisory-only: SessionStart, Setup, PostToolUse, PostToolUseFailure, PermissionDenied, SubagentStart, FileChanged, CwdChanged, InstructionsLoaded, WorktreeCreate (non-zero fails creation but hook REPLACES git — it must create the worktree itself), WorktreeRemove, StopFailure, Notification, MessageDisplay, PostCompact, SessionEnd. => Catalog all 30 events in your enforcement documentation. When choosing an event for a new control, prefer advisory events (SessionStart, PostToolUse, PostCompact) for context injection and alerting; reserve blocking events (PreToolUse, PreCompact, ConfigChange) for hard security gates where a false-positive is acceptable. Never add decision:block to PostToolUse — it is advisory-only; use PostToolBatch instead to halt the agentic loop before the next model call.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] SessionStart fires on session startup, resume, /clear, and post-compact. It is non-blocking (exit code ignored). Its hookSpecificOutput supports additionalContext (injected as a system reminder before the first model request — not a chat message), initialUserMessage (first user turn in -p non-interactive mode only), sessionTitle (auto-name session), watchPaths (files to watch for FileChanged), and reloadSkills. The source field in JSON input distinguishes startup vs resume vs compact, enabling targeted reground logic. CLAUDE_ENV_FILE allows persisting env vars for subsequent Bash tool calls. => Wire a SessionStart hook that reads docs/canon/BINDING_RULES.md and emits additionalContext with BR-0..BR-21 summary + anticheat stance on every startup and resume. Use source == 'compact' match to re-inject the full CONSTRAINTS.md after compaction (supplements PostCompact). On Ultron, also dump E:\UltronModels inventory and current config.yaml hash so Claude is grounded without needing a separate read. Windows snippet: { "SessionStart": [{ "hooks": [{ "type": "command", "command": "node ${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/hooks/session-start.js", "timeout": 30 }] }] }
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] UserPromptSubmit fires before Claude processes the user prompt, receives the prompt text in JSON input, and supports both decision:block (to reject the prompt and erase it) and additionalContext (injected alongside the prompt for Claude to see). Using only additionalContext (never decision:block) turns this event into a zero-blocking context injector. Default timeout is 30 seconds (shorter than the standard 600s). The prompt field in JSON input enables pattern-matching for advisory routing. => Use UserPromptSubmit with additionalContext-only (no decision:block path) to prepend a one-line reminder of the active anticheat posture and current flavor state to every turn on Ultron. For the Kit, use it to inject a brief CONSTRAINTS.md summary hash so Claude can self-check without re-reading files. Keep the hook under 5 seconds to stay within the 30s timeout. Do NOT use decision:block here for automated blocking — that creates confirmation fatigue if it fires on legitimate maintenance prompts like 'edit BINDING_RULES.md'.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] PostToolUse is advisory-only: it fires AFTER the tool has already executed, so exit 2 cannot undo the side effect. It can return updatedToolOutput to rewrite what Claude sees as the tool result (useful for redacting secrets from Read output), and additionalContext to inject advisory information. It CANNOT stop the agentic loop before the next model call — use PostToolBatch for that. PostToolBatch fires once per parallel batch BEFORE the next model call and supports decision:block to halt the loop, making it the correct hook for post-execution quality gates. => Wire PostToolUse with matcher 'Read|Bash' to scan tool output for secrets (API keys, passwords, GGUF model paths you don't want in the transcript) and return updatedToolOutput with redacted text. This is zero-blocking-risk because the tool already ran. Wire PostToolBatch for post-batch quality gates if you need to halt the loop after a bad batch — but be aware that false-positives here will interrupt autonomous workflows.
- [HOOK|both|risk:med|high] Stop hook self-deadlock: a Stop hook that always returns exit 2 or decision:block loops forever, because each block causes Claude to continue and fire the Stop hook again. The canonical prevention is the stop_hook_active boolean field in the Stop hook's JSON input. When true, the hook is already in a 'forced continuation' state from a prior block; the hook MUST exit 0 immediately. This field is also present in SubagentStop input (confirmed in SDK TypeScript example: subInput.stop_hook_active). A Stop hook that ignores this flag and always blocks is a fatal harness failure. => Every Stop hook must begin with: if (input.stop_hook_active) { process.exit(0); }. Scope Stop hooks narrowly — check only files changed in the current turn (read transcript_path to find current-turn edits). Back Stop hook logic with CI so the same check runs in pipeline and the Stop hook serves as a runtime echo, not the sole enforcement. Treat stop_hook_active=true as a FATAL override signal — log it but do not block.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] PreCompact fires before context compaction (manual /compact or auto-triggered), supports decision:block to abort compaction, and matchers 'manual' vs 'auto' allow selective behavior. PostCompact fires after compaction completes, is advisory-only (cannot block), and is the correct place to re-inject grounding context via additionalContext. PreCompact with only file-snapshot side-effects (no decision:block) is zero-blocking-risk and valuable for preserving state (STATUS.md, current CONSTRAINTS.md snapshot) before turns are summarized away. => Wire a PreCompact hook (both matchers, no decision:block) that: (1) copies STATUS.md to .claude/snapshots/STATUS_precompact_<timestamp>.md, (2) writes current config.yaml hash to .claude/snapshots/config_hash.txt. Wire a PostCompact hook that emits additionalContext re-injecting the CONSTRAINTS.md summary so Claude is re-grounded immediately after compaction. Both hooks are zero-blocking-risk.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] SubagentStop fires when a subagent finishes. Its JSON input includes agent_id, agent_type, agent_transcript_path, and stop_hook_active. It supports decision:block (preventing the subagent from stopping) but using it without checking stop_hook_active causes the same deadlock as Stop. The SDK agent example shows stop_hook_active on SubagentStop input explicitly. A Stop hook registered inside a subagent's config is automatically treated as SubagentStop when that agent runs as a subagent — no manual wiring needed. => Use SubagentStop with zero-blocking (no decision:block) for: (1) aggregating subagent results by reading agent_transcript_path and appending to a shared log, (2) audit-trailing every spawned agent with agent_id/agent_type. For Ultron's multi-agent workflows (wakeword intent gate + 8B LLM pipeline), SubagentStop is the correct place to log when each subagent phase completes without risking blocking the orchestration loop.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] WorktreeCreate REPLACES the default git worktree creation behavior — Claude Code does not run git itself; the hook IS responsible for creating the worktree and must print the worktree path to stdout (for command hooks) or return hookSpecificOutput.worktreePath (for HTTP hooks). Any non-zero exit fails creation entirely. This fires when --worktree or isolation:worktree is used. WorktreeRemove is advisory-only (exit code ignored) and fires after removal for cleanup. => For Ultron, wire a WorktreeCreate command hook that: (1) runs git worktree add <generated-path> <branch>, (2) prints the path to stdout. This lets you enforce naming conventions (e.g. .claude/worktrees/<slug>-<ts>) and log each worktree creation. Wire WorktreeRemove (advisory) to clean up any symlinks or logs. The Kit should provide a template WorktreeCreate hook that auto-names and auto-branches. Note: if you have no WorktreeCreate hook, the default git behavior runs — the hook only activates when you register one.
- [CONFIG|ultron|risk:none|high] On Windows 11, hooks can declare shell:powershell in the hook config to run PowerShell commands directly. However, shell:powershell is IGNORED when the args field is set (exec form bypasses shell). Node.js is the most portable hook runtime for Windows because Claude Code itself requires Node.js (it is always on PATH). The if field in hook config uses permission-rule syntax (e.g. Bash(git *), Edit(*.ts)) to filter which tool calls trigger the hook — evaluated only on tool events (PreToolUse, PostToolUse, PostToolUseFailure, PermissionRequest, PermissionDenied); on other events a hook with if set never runs. => For Ultron (Windows 11), write all hook scripts as Node.js .js files in .claude/hooks/. Use shell:powershell only for trivial one-liners. Avoid bash+jq — they may not be present. Use the if field to narrow expensive hooks: e.g. if:"Bash" on a command-scanner hook so it only runs for Bash tool calls, not Read/Grep/etc. This reduces hook overhead on the 10,700-line orchestrator edit loops. Example narrowing: { "if": "Bash", "type": "command", "command": "node .claude/hooks/bash-scanner.js" }.
PITFALLS: Stop hook deadlock: a Stop hook that returns decision:block without checking stop_hook_active loops forever. This is not theoretical — it is a well-documented production failure mode. Every Stop hook must exit 0 immediately when stop_hook_active is true in JSON input. | PostToolUse is advisory, not a gate: developers commonly assume PostToolUse can block or undo the tool's side effect. It cannot. The tool has already executed. Use PreToolUse for pre-execution gates and PostToolBatch if you need to halt the loop after a batch completes. | WorktreeCreate replaces git, not supplements it: if you register a WorktreeCreate hook you are responsible for running git worktree add yourself and printing the path to stdout. Forgetting to print the path causes worktree creation to fail silently with a non-informative error. | ConfigChange cannot block policy_settings: a ConfigChange hook with exit 2 can block user_settings / project_settings / local_settings / skills but cannot block managed policy_settings. Policy settings are admin-controlled and bypass hook blocking by design. | shell:powershell is ignored when args field is set: on Windows, if you use exec-form hooks (with an args array), the shell property is silently ignored. Use Node.js command hooks for cross-form compatibility. | UserPromptSubmit has a 30-second timeout vs the standard 600s for other hooks. A slow hook here (e.g. embedding lookup, LLM call) will timeout and may surface confusing errors or be skipped. | InstructionsLoaded is observe-only: it fires when CLAUDE.md or .claude/rules/*.md loads but cannot inject additionalContext or block the load. Use SessionStart additionalContext for grounding injection instead. | PostCompact is advisory-only: despite being the obvious place to re-inject grounding after compaction, PostCompact cannot block or force Claude to re-read files. It can only emit additionalContext — which IS useful but must be kept short since the context window is already under pressure post-compaction. | Multiple hooks run in parallel per event: if you register multiple PreToolUse hooks, they all run concurrently and the most restrictive result wins (deny beats ask beats allow beats defer). A hook that always denies will override all other hooks' allow decisions, creating a silent blackhole. Always log permissionDecisionReason. | The 'if' field only works on tool events: if you put an 'if' filter on a SessionStart or PreCompact hook entry, the hook never runs. The if field is only evaluated for PreToolUse, PostToolUse, PostToolUseFailure, PermissionRequest, and PermissionDenied. | Async hook output cannot block: returning { async: true } from a hook callback tells the agent to proceed immediately. Async hooks cannot inject additionalContext, block, or modify inputs. Use them only for fire-and-forget side effects (logging, Slack notifications).
OPENQ: Is stop_hook_active present in the Stop event's shell command hook JSON input (settings.json hooks), or only in SDK callback hooks? The official hooks page (code.claude.com/docs/en/hooks) did not explicitly show it in the Stop shell-command input schema, but the Agent SDK docs (code.claude.com/docs/en/agent-sdk/hooks) confirm it in the SubagentStop TypeScript example. Needs verification against the full Stop event schema in the hooks reference. | PostToolUse decision:block — conflicting signals across sources. The morphllm.com source (based on the official docs) shows PostToolUse in the decision:block table but the behavior is 'shows stderr to Claude (tool already ran)'. The Agent SDK docs say PostToolUse additionalContext appends to tool result but does not mention decision:block halting the loop. Does PostToolUse decision:block actually stop the agentic loop before the next model call, or is it truly advisory (just feeds reason to Claude)? The answer determines whether PostToolUse can serve as a loop-halt gate. | WorktreeCreate: is the hook responsible for creating the worktree only when explicitly registered, or does Claude Code always call the hook and skip git if a hook is present? If no WorktreeCreate hook is registered, does Claude Code fall back to default git worktree add behavior? | InstructionsLoaded: the docs say it is observe-only with no decision control. Is there any hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext supported on this event? If so, it would allow augmenting every CLAUDE.md load with enforcement reminders. | ConfigChange blocking granularity: can a ConfigChange hook selectively block only certain config keys (e.g., block changes to denyTools but allow changes to model), or is the block all-or-nothing for the entire config_source file? | PreToolUse permissionDecision:defer semantics in the Agent SDK context: 'defer ends the query so you can resume it later' — does this mean the entire agentic session pauses, or only the current tool call? How does resume work in practice for the Ultron single-GPU single-session setup? | Does the 'matcher' field on SessionStart / PreCompact / PostCompact hooks (which are not tool events) use the same permission-rule syntax, or does it match against event-specific fields like the source (startup|resume|compact) or trigger (manual|auto)?

### exit codes vs JSON output — advisory vs blocking control
Claude Code hooks offer two orthogonal blocking axes — exit code (2 = hard block, 0 = process JSON, other = non-blocking warn) and JSON payload (permissionDecision allow/deny/ask/defer, decision:block, continue:false) — plus three advisory-only channels (additionalContext, systemMessage, updatedToolOutput). The canonical decision tree is: use permissionDecision:deny or exit 2 for hard security policy; use updatedInput to silently rewrite dangerous args into safe ones; use additionalContext/systemMessage for guidance with no friction; use updatedToolOutput to scrub secrets from model context post-execution; use decision:block on Stop only with a termination guard against self-deadlock. Two open bugs (as of v2.1.119) affect the interaction between permissionDecision:allow and native prompts, and between permissionDecision:ask and permissions.deny rules — both are tracked in official GitHub issues. For Ultron/Kenning specifically, all hooks should be authored as Node.js scripts (guaranteed on-path since Claude Code requires it) or PowerShell, not bash+jq, to ensure Windows compatibility.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] Exit code 2 is the coarse hard-block: for PreToolUse, UserPromptSubmit, Stop, SubagentStop, PreCompact, ConfigChange, WorktreeCreate, TeammateIdle, TaskCreated, TaskCompleted the tool call (or session stop) is cancelled and stderr is injected into the model's context as an error message. Exit code 1 (and all other non-zero, non-2 codes) is NON-blocking: Claude Code logs a notice in the transcript and continues. Exit 0 triggers JSON parsing from stdout. These are mutually exclusive: Claude Code IGNORES stdout JSON when exit code is 2. => Use exit 2 exclusively for unambiguous hard security denials where no context is needed (e.g., anticheat firewall detecting a blocklisted import, or a known-destructive shell pattern). Do NOT use exit 1 thinking it blocks — it does not. Never return JSON on exit 2; it is ignored.
- [HOOK|ultron|risk:low|high] permissionDecision (PreToolUse JSON output, exit 0) is the fine-grained permission layer with four values: 'allow' (bypass permission prompt), 'deny' (block with reason sent to model), 'ask' (interactive user prompt — NOTE: open bug #39344 where it silently overrides permissions.deny rules), 'defer' (pause for headless --resume flow). Priority when multiple PreToolUse hooks fire in parallel: deny > defer > ask > allow. A single deny from any hook blocks the call regardless of what other hooks return. => For Ultron: use 'deny' (not exit 2) when you need to communicate the reason to the model so it adapts (e.g., 'use run_tests.py not pytest'). Use 'allow' to auto-approve read-only tools. AVOID 'ask' for any command also covered by a permissions.deny rule — bug #39344 means the deny rule is silently bypassed. Do not rely on 'allow' suppressing the native prompt in interactive mode — bug #52822 shows it may still appear in v2.1.119.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] updatedInput (inside hookSpecificOutput, PreToolUse only, exit 0) rewrites the tool's arguments before execution. Must be paired with permissionDecision:'allow' or 'ask' — it is ignored with 'deny' or 'defer'. updatedInput replaces the ENTIRE tool_input object, so always spread the original and mutate only the target field. This enables silent arg sanitization without blocking. The rewritten command bypasses the interactive permission prompt when paired with 'allow', so rewriting logic is the highest-security code in the hook set. => Use updatedInput for safe auto-correction: downgrade 'git push --force' to '--force-with-lease', redirect file writes to sandboxed paths, inject required test flags. Pair with additionalContext to inform the model of the rewrite so it does not retry with original args.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] updatedToolOutput (PostToolUse hookSpecificOutput, exit 0) replaces the tool's output before the model sees it. It does NOT undo execution. Use it to redact secrets, PII, or oversized outputs from the model's context without affecting the actual file or command result. The field is capped at 10,000 characters. additionalContext (also PostToolUse) APPENDS advisory context to the tool result — it cannot block and the tool output is unchanged. => Use updatedToolOutput on PostToolUse Bash/Read hooks to scrub API keys, tokens, and .env secrets from shell output before they enter the model's context. For Ultron: scrub any Read or Bash output that may echo KENNING_ env var values or config.yaml secrets. Pair with suppressOutput:true if the hook's own stdout is also sensitive.
- [HOOK|ultron|risk:med|high] Stop and SubagentStop hooks receive stop_hook_active:true in their JSON input when the Stop hook itself is the reason Claude is trying to stop again (i.e., the hook blocked the previous stop, Claude did more work, and now it is trying to stop again). Failing to check stop_hook_active creates a hard infinite loop. The official docs warn that 'a Stop hook that always returns decision:block never lets Claude stop.' stop_hook_active is a field in the hook input JSON, not an environment variable. => ALL Stop/SubagentStop hooks that ever return decision:block MUST gate on stop_hook_active first. Pattern: if (input.stop_hook_active) process.exit(0). For Ultron: use a Stop hook to enforce 'tests must pass before session ends' with exactly one block per session using the stop_hook_active guard. Never deploy a Stop hook without this guard.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] continue:false (top-level JSON field, any event, exit 0) is a session kill: it halts Claude Code entirely, showing stopReason to the user, and takes priority over all other decision fields including decision:block. suppressOutput:true hides the hook's own stdout from the transcript (but not debug logs). systemMessage (top-level) shows a string to the human operator in the terminal — it does NOT inject into the model's context. additionalContext (inside hookSpecificOutput) injects into the model's context — advisory only, no block. These serve different audiences: continue:false=session kill, suppressOutput=transcript hygiene, systemMessage=human alert, additionalContext=model guidance. => For the Frontier Kit: use systemMessage in a UserPromptSubmit hook to warn the human operator of policy violations without blocking autonomous work. Use additionalContext in PostToolUse/PostToolBatch hooks for non-blocking model reminders. Reserve continue:false for genuine emergencies only (e.g., detected credential exfiltration). Never use continue:false as a substitute for permissionDecision:deny on a single tool call.
- [HOOK|ultron|risk:none|high] PostToolUse does NOT support exit 2 blocking — the tool has already executed. PostToolUse CAN return decision:block+reason, but this is advisory: it forces the model to address the issue in its next response but CANNOT undo execution. PostToolBatch (fires once after all tools in a batch resolve, before the next model call) also supports decision:block and is the correct hook for batch-level policy (e.g., 'you edited 5 files but ran no tests'). Events with zero blocking capability (side effects only): SessionEnd, WorktreeRemove, CwdChanged, FileChanged, PostCompact, InstructionsLoaded, Notification, MessageDisplay (MessageDisplay can only change displayed text, not the transcript). => Use PostToolBatch (not PostToolUse loop) when you want to inject a policy reminder after a cluster of edits — it fires once per batch. Use PostToolUse:decision:block only as a 'soft veto with explanation' when the model must re-evaluate its last action. For Ultron: a PostToolBatch hook that detects orchestrator.py edits without a codebase_structure.md update and injects additionalContext is the correct advisory pattern (BR-21.4).
- [CONFIG|ultron|risk:none|high] For Windows (Ultron/Kenning), hooks declared with 'shell':'powershell' run under PowerShell. Node.js is universally available because Claude Code itself requires it, making it the most portable hook runtime on Windows. bash+jq are NOT guaranteed on Windows. $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR resolves the project root. PowerShell hooks must use [Console]::Error.WriteLine() for stderr and Write-Output for stdout JSON. JSON output must be UTF-8 without BOM. Hook scripts must use absolute paths via $env:CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR. => Author all Ultron hooks as Node.js scripts (.js) invoked via 'node $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/hooks/hook_name.js' in the command field, with no shell declared. Node is the safest cross-env runtime on Windows. Fallback to PowerShell only for hooks needing PS-native features. Store all hook scripts under .claude/hooks/ and reference them via $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR.
- [HOOK|both|risk:high|high] The 'ask' vs 'defer' distinction is critical for headless/subagent use. 'ask' surfaces an interactive terminal permission prompt to the human user and resumes inline. 'defer' causes Claude Code to EXIT with stop_reason:'tool_deferred' and the pending tool call preserved in the transcript; the calling process reads deferred_tool_use from the SDK result, handles the decision in its own UI, then calls claude -p --resume <session-id> to continue. Returning 'defer' from a hook ENDS the current query — it is not a pause, it is an exit. This is documented in GitHub issue #41791 which notes that the hooks docs omit the defer behavior for headless --resume flows. => For Ultron (always interactive, never headless): never use 'defer' — it would terminate the session. Use 'ask' sparingly for non-security-critical gates where human judgment is genuinely needed and no deny rule covers the same command (to avoid the #39344 bug interaction). For both: use 'deny' for hard security policy, 'allow' for pre-approved operations, 'ask' only as a last resort.
PITFALLS: Exit code 2 and JSON stdout are mutually exclusive: Claude Code ignores JSON output when exit code is 2. Mixing them (returning a JSON body AND exit 2) silently discards the JSON — the common mistake when porting bash scripts that echo JSON and then exit 2. | Bug #39344 (open as of research date): permissionDecision:'ask' silently overrides permissions.deny rules — a command explicitly denied in settings.json can execute if any PreToolUse hook returns 'ask' for it. Never return 'ask' for commands covered by deny rules. | Bug #52822 (regression from v2.1.59, present in v2.1.119): permissionDecision:'allow' does not suppress the native interactive permission prompt even though the JSON is parsed successfully. Programmatic auto-approval workflows may not work reliably in interactive mode. | Stop hook self-deadlock: any Stop hook that unconditionally returns decision:block creates an infinite loop. MUST check input.stop_hook_active and exit 0 when true. Never use exit 2 in a Stop hook block response — exit 0 with JSON decision:block is correct. | continue:false is a session kill, not a tool veto. Using it as a substitute for permissionDecision:deny on a single tool call will abort all unrelated work in the same session. | updatedInput with permissionDecision:'allow' bypasses the interactive permission prompt entirely — the rewritten command executes with no human review. A logic error in a rewriting hook silently grants unintended access. | PostToolUse decision:block is advisory, not a true block. The tool has already executed; decision:block only forces the model to address the issue in its next response and cannot undo the write/execute. | additionalContext is capped at 10,000 characters. For large structured data (test reports, diffs), write to a file and inject the path as additionalContext rather than the full content. | Multiple PreToolUse hooks fire in parallel; completion order is non-deterministic. Do not write hooks that rely on another hook having run first. | The 'defer' permissionDecision ENDS the current query with stop_reason:tool_deferred. In interactive Ultron sessions this would terminate the session unexpectedly. Reserve 'defer' exclusively for headless --resume pipeline integrations.
OPENQ: Is bug #39344 (permissionDecision:'ask' bypassing permissions.deny) fixed in any released version after the research date? The issue was marked Critical but no fix commit was cited in the fetched thread. | Is bug #52822 (permissionDecision:'allow' not suppressing native prompt in interactive mode v2.1.119) fixed in a later patch? The issue notes it was working in v2.1.59, implying a regression. | Does stop_hook_active propagate correctly to SubagentStop hooks, or only to Stop hooks? The SDK docs show stop_hook_active on SubagentStop input but the deadlock risk for SubagentStop-level looping is not explicitly documented. | What is the exact JSON shape of tool_response in PostToolUse input for non-Bash tools (Read, WebFetch) — is updatedToolOutput a plain string or must it be a typed block object ({ type:'text', text:'...' })? | Can a PermissionRequest hook's updatedInput modification be seen by a subsequent PreToolUse hook for the same tool call, or do the two hooks see independent snapshots of the original input? | Are hook scripts in .claude/hooks/ automatically included when the Frontier Kit is dropped into a new project, or must the hooks field in settings.json be manually re-configured per project? | For PostToolBatch, what is the exact shape of input.tool_calls — is it an array of { tool_name, tool_input } objects, or does it match a different schema than individual PreToolUse inputs?

### Stop/SubagentStop hook without self-deadlock
The Stop hook fires when Claude finishes a turn; returning decision:"block" (exit 0 + JSON) or exiting with code 2 forces a continuation, creating infinite-loop risk if the blocking condition is never resolved. The canonical prevention mechanism is the stop_hook_active boolean in the hook's stdin JSON: it is true on a Stop/SubagentStop invocation that itself exists only because a prior block was issued, signaling the hook must exit 0 unconditionally. The harness additionally enforces a hard block cap (default 8 consecutive blocks; overridable via CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP env var) after which the turn ends regardless of hook output — treat this override as a FATAL signal and log it. Real-world infinite-loop incidents were caused by: (1) ignoring stop_hook_active, (2) blocking on a condition that can never be satisfied (e.g., referencing unregistered skills, or an async background agent that hasn't completed), and (3) returning {"continue":true} unconditionally. Safe pattern: check stop_hook_active first and exit 0 immediately when true; scope validation to files git-changed in the current turn (git diff --name-only HEAD) to avoid re-checking stale state; prefer Node.js over PowerShell/bash for Windows because a confirmed Windows bug (issue #46601) causes pwsh Stop hooks to receive empty stdin. Back Stop hooks with CI so they never need to be the last line of defense. Treat any block-cap override as a fatal enforcement failure requiring CI-level alerting.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] stop_hook_active is a boolean field in the Stop/SubagentStop stdin JSON that is set to true when the current stop attempt was itself generated because a prior Stop hook returned decision:block. Checking this flag and exiting 0 immediately when true is the ONLY documented, harness-enforced mechanism for preventing a single hook from looping forever. If a hook ignores this flag, the loop continues until the block cap is hit. => Make stop_hook_active the very first check in every Stop and SubagentStop hook script, before any I/O or validation. Exit 0 immediately when true. Never block when stop_hook_active is true.
- [CI|both|risk:none|med] Claude Code enforces a hard block cap: after a Stop hook blocks 8 consecutive times without progress, the harness overrides the block and forces the turn to end regardless of hook output. The cap is configurable via the CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP environment variable. Do NOT hardcode the count of 8 into hook logic — the cap may change and is separate from stop_hook_active. Treat a cap override as a FATAL enforcement failure. => Do not hardcode the count 8. Set CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP in your environment if you have a legitimately long convergence loop. Log to stderr when your hook would have blocked so that a cap override shows up in the debug log as an anomaly. Route cap-override events to a CI alert.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] Exit code 2 and exit 0 + JSON {decision:"block"} are both blocking for Stop/SubagentStop, but they behave differently: exit 2 routes stderr directly to Claude as feedback and blocks; exit 0 + JSON gives structured control where the reason field is shown to the user and to Claude. Exit code 1 (conventional Unix failure) is treated as NON-blocking — Claude proceeds despite it. This is a widely observed gotcha that silently allows Claude to stop when the intent was to block. => Always use exit 0 + JSON {decision:"block", reason:"..."} for Stop hooks — it gives Claude an actionable reason, avoids the exit-1 silent-pass trap, and keeps stdout/stderr clean for structured output. Reserve exit 2 only when you need unconditional blocking without a structured reason (e.g., a watchdog that should never be bypassed).
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] Scoping Stop hook validation to files changed in the CURRENT TURN (via git diff --name-only HEAD) prevents re-running expensive checks on unchanged files, avoids false blocks from pre-existing failures unrelated to Claude's work, and makes the block reason actionable. The transcript_path field in the Stop hook input provides the session transcript for audit, not for determining changed files — git is the right tool for scoping. => In the Stop hook, run `git diff --name-only HEAD` (or `git status --porcelain`) filtered to the project root to get the turn's changed file set. Only block if the CHANGED files fail the check. Pass the file list in the reason field so Claude knows exactly what to fix.
- [HOOK|ultron|risk:med|high] A confirmed Windows-specific bug (GitHub issue #46601, closed as not-planned, Claude Code v2.1.101+) causes Stop hooks invoked via `pwsh -File ...` or `powershell.exe -File ...` to receive EMPTY stdin — IsInputRedirected returns False inside the script. This means stop_hook_active, cwd, and all other context fields are unavailable, making the hook unable to function as a structural safety gate on Windows. The same issue does NOT affect UserPromptSubmit hooks under identical configuration. => On Windows (Ultron), invoke Stop hooks via `node .claude/hooks/stop-gate.mjs` — not via pwsh or powershell.exe. Node.js is guaranteed available on every Claude Code installation, handles stdin reliably, and is cross-platform. Use fs.readFileSync(0, 'utf8') with a try/catch fallback to {} for cases where stdin is empty or not yet piped.
- [ADVISORY|both|risk:none|high] SubagentStop is identical to Stop in output schema and exit-code behavior, but receives agent_id and agent_type fields instead of permission_mode. It fires when a subagent finishes, NOT when the main agent finishes. If you only register a Stop hook, subagent completions are not gated. Deadlock prevention is identical: check stop_hook_active, exit 0 when true. Use the agent_type matcher to scope SubagentStop hooks to specific agent types (e.g., security-reviewer) to avoid firing on every subagent. => Register SubagentStop separately from Stop if you need quality gates on subagents. Use the agent_type matcher to narrow scope. Reuse the same stop_hook_active guard. For Ultron (no multi-agent today but the canon calls for future subagents), register a SubagentStop hook that at minimum logs agent_id + agent_type for audit and exits 0 without blocking — add blocking only when a specific gate is needed.
- [ADVISORY|both|risk:high|high] Real-world infinite-loop incidents documented in anthropics/claude-code issues #55754 and #58348 share a common pattern: blocking on a condition that CANNOT be satisfied during the current continuation (async background agents not yet completed; skills not registered in the session; unresolvable verification artifact). The block cap eventually fires but only after consuming significant tokens (50+ minutes, 100+ iterations in the wild). The correct fix is to make the blocking condition satisfiable within one continuation, or to return additionalContext (non-blocking advisory) instead of decision:block when the missing condition is outside Claude's control. => Before registering a blocking Stop hook, verify that the condition being checked IS something Claude can resolve in one continuation. If the gate depends on external state (background task completion, external service, async CI), use additionalContext (non-blocking) instead of decision:block, or add an explicit unsatisfiable-condition exit: if the condition has been blocked N times with no git diff change since the last block, emit decision:block with reason 'no progress detected — override if intentional' and log a FATAL-level warning.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] The Stop hook additionalContext path (hookSpecificOutput.hookEventName:Stop + additionalContext) is non-blocking: Claude receives the context as a system reminder on the next turn but the current turn ends. This is suitable for injecting audit info, git state, or test-result summaries without creating loop risk. It is strictly advisory and MUST NOT be used as a substitute for a real block when a hard gate is needed — but it is far safer than decision:block for routine telemetry. => Use additionalContext for informational post-turn injection (branch name, uncommitted file count, test-pass summary). Use decision:block ONLY for conditions Claude can actively fix in the next continuation. Never mix both in the same JSON object — the decision field takes precedence and the block fires even if you included additionalContext.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] Multiple Claude Code hook issues (#10412, #12667, #34600) document that Stop hook exit 2 was at one point silently ignored or displayed as 'error' instead of triggering a block. The recommended canonical form is exit 0 + JSON {decision:"block", reason:"..."} which has been stable across Claude Code versions. Exit 2 remains available but the UX display and version stability are inferior. For the Frontier Kit which targets many unknown Claude Code versions, exit 0 + JSON is the only portable form. => Standardize all Stop and SubagentStop blocking on exit 0 + JSON {decision:"block", reason:"..."} in both the project-specific Ultron hooks and the portable Frontier Kit hooks. Never rely on exit 2 as the primary blocking mechanism for Stop. If exit 2 is used as a fallback watchdog, document that it may display as 'error' in the UI.
PITFALLS: stop_hook_active does NOT prevent loops automatically — the flag is passed in and your code must check it. If you forget the check or misread the field name, the loop runs until the block cap fires. | The block cap default of 8 is NOT documented on an official page that was directly confirmed by fetch — it was corroborated by multiple secondary sources. Do not hardcode 8 into hook logic; use stop_hook_active instead, which is harness-enforced. | exit 1 from a Stop hook is silently non-blocking — Claude proceeds. This contradicts Unix convention and causes silent governance failures if developers instinctively use exit 1 for errors. | Windows pwsh/PowerShell Stop hooks receive empty stdin (confirmed bug #46601, closed not-planned). Any Stop hook that parses stdin JSON and falls back to {} will appear to work but will never see stop_hook_active:true — it will always see the zero-value false equivalent of an empty object. This means the stop_hook_active guard silently does nothing on Windows with pwsh hooks, so the guard only works if the hook itself runs under Node.js. | Blocking on unsatisfiable conditions (external async state, unregistered skills, missing CI artifacts) causes the loop to run until the block cap override fires — consuming tokens and potentially hitting billing limits. The block cap override is not a graceful exit. | Multiple Stop hooks in the same event all run in parallel; if ANY returns decision:block, Claude retries. A partially-working hook that sometimes blocks and sometimes doesn't creates non-deterministic behavior. The block cap counter applies per-session, not per-hook. | additionalContext and decision:block must NOT be combined in the same JSON root object — the decision field takes precedence and the block fires even if you intended advisory-only behavior. | The continue:true field in hook output (documented as a separate field from decision:block) can also trigger infinite loops — confirmed in claude-mem issue #1288. Do not use continue:true in Stop hooks. | Stop hook timeout: if the hook command itself hangs (e.g., a test runner that never completes), Claude Code waits indefinitely. Always set a timeout in the hook configuration and use the Node.js AbortSignal or a process-level timeout to ensure the hook exits within the configured window. | SubagentStop with a broad or empty matcher fires on EVERY subagent completion including background utility agents. A blocking SubagentStop with a broad matcher can deadlock multi-agent workflows. Always use the agent_type matcher to scope SubagentStop hooks.
OPENQ: Is the block cap default of 8 officially documented anywhere on code.claude.com/docs? Multiple secondary sources assert 8 and CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP, but the primary fetch of the official hooks reference did not surface this text verbatim. Verify by fetching code.claude.com/docs/en/hooks directly when this is an active concern. | Does Node.js via `node hook.mjs` fully resolve the Windows stdin-empty issue for Stop hooks (#46601), or is the stdin-empty bug at the harness level affecting all hook types on certain Windows configurations? The bug report only tested pwsh; Node.js immunity was asserted by secondary sources but not confirmed with a direct repro. | When stop_hook_active is true and the hook exits 0, does the block cap counter reset for the next turn, or does it persist across turns? This matters for long-running sessions where Stop hooks may legitimately block on multiple separate turns. | Does decision:block in a Stop hook interact with /stop or Ctrl+C user overrides? The official docs say user Ctrl+C bypasses all hooks immediately, but this has not been confirmed when the Stop hook itself is in a block loop. | For Ultron specifically: the test runner wrapper is `scripts/run_tests.py --stale-heartbeat=400` — if a Stop hook invokes this wrapper to gate on test passage, what is the worst-case execution time, and does that exceed the hook timeout? The timeout field in the hook configuration needs to be explicitly set above that worst-case. | Is additionalContext in a SubagentStop hook surfaced to the PARENT agent, to the subagent, or to both? The docs say it is 'injected as a system reminder on the next turn' but it is ambiguous which session's next turn receives it in a multi-agent workflow.

### robust PreToolUse dangerous-command blocking
PreToolUse hooks with permissionDecision:"deny" are the correct enforcement layer for blocking dangerous git/shell commands in Claude Code. The official docs confirm: (1) permissionDecision:"deny" works even in --dangerously-skip-permissions / bypassPermissions mode because hooks execute before the permission bypass is consulted; (2) the "if" field does real subcommand parsing (strips leading VAR=, walks &&/;/|, enters $() and backticks) but FAILS OPEN when parsing fails — making it unsuitable as the sole gate; (3) the robust pattern is a Node.js hook (always available on Windows since Claude Code requires Node) that reads the full command from stdin JSON, applies word-boundary regex per flag, and emits hookSpecificOutput/permissionDecision:"deny" on exit 0 — never rely on exit 2 alone because exit 2 ignores any JSON stdout and cannot inject additionalContext; (4) false positives from quoted strings require explicit quote-stripping before flag scanning; (5) hooks FAIL OPEN on crashes, missing deps, or any exit code other than 2, so the hook must catch all exceptions and default to deny on error for security-critical gates.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] permissionDecision:"deny" in hookSpecificOutput blocks the tool call even when --dangerously-skip-permissions or bypassPermissions mode is active. The flag skips interactive confirmation prompts, not hook execution. => Always use hookSpecificOutput / permissionDecision:"deny" (not just exit 2) for security-critical blocks so (a) the deny reason is fedback to Claude, (b) additionalContext can guide the next turn, and (c) the block survives bypass-mode automation. Wire via exit 0 + JSON stdout, not exit 2.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] The "if" field performs real shell-aware subcommand parsing: it strips leading VAR=value assignments, independently checks each subcommand separated by &&, ;, or |, and descends into $() and backtick expressions. However, the official docs state explicitly: "The filter also fails open, running your hook regardless of pattern, when the Bash command cannot be parsed." => Use the "if" field only as a performance optimization (skip hook spawn on obviously irrelevant commands), NEVER as the security gate itself. Put the actual block logic inside the hook script. For the dangerous-git hook, omit "if" entirely or use a broad "if":"Bash(git *)" to reduce spawns, but do the real regex check in Node.js.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] Exit code semantics: exit 0 + JSON stdout = structured decision (allow/deny/ask/defer); exit 2 = immediate block, stderr fed to Claude, JSON ignored; any other exit code = NON-BLOCKING error, Claude Code proceeds. This means exit 1 (the conventional Unix error) is fail-OPEN. A crashing hook that exits uncleanly also fails open. => In the Node.js hook, wrap the entire body in try/catch and always call deny() in the catch block. Never let the process exit with code 1 or via an uncaught exception. Test that the hook still denies when fed malformed JSON. Do NOT use exit 2 as the primary block path for dangerous-git — it silently discards the permissionDecisionReason and additionalContext that guide Claude's retry.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] False positives arise when dangerous flag tokens appear inside quoted strings or as path components. A regex like /--force/ matches git commit -m "--force is bad" and a path like /my--force-tool/push. Naively blocking on flag presence causes friction with legitimate commits that mention these flags in messages. => Before flag-scanning, strip single-quoted and double-quoted substrings from the command copy (replace /'[^']*'|"[^"]*"/g with empty strings). This prevents quoted commit messages, path arguments, and string literals from triggering blocks. Then apply word-boundary regexes (\b) on the stripped copy. Retain the original command for logging/context.
- [HOOK|ultron|risk:none|high] On Windows, hook commands that rely on bash, sh, or jq are unreliable. Git Bash may not be in PATH, variable expansion is mangled when bash is invoked by Claude Code's Node runtime, and .sh scripts need LF line endings (git core.autocrlf=true converts to CRLF causing 'bad interpreter' errors). Node.js is ALWAYS available on every Claude Code platform because Claude Code requires it. => For Ultron/Windows: declare the hook as "command":"node", "args":["${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/hooks/block-dangerous-git.js"]. Do NOT use shell form or "shell":"powershell" for security gates (PowerShell adds startup latency and variable-expansion bugs documented in Feb 2026). Use path.join() and os.homedir() inside the script for any path construction. Add .gitattributes: *.sh text eol=lf if any bash hooks exist elsewhere in the repo.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] Interpreter-bypass vulnerability: a regex on the raw Bash command string cannot catch dangerous operations wrapped inside an interpreter invocation. Commands like `python -c "import os; os.system('git push --force')"` or `node -e "require('child_process').execSync('git reset --hard HEAD')"` launch the interpreter cleanly, and the destructive operation happens at interpreter runtime — invisible to the hook's string scan. => Treat the hook as defence-in-depth, not a hermetic seal. Additionally: (1) add a deny rule in settings.json for `python -c`, `node -e`, `bash -c` with embedded git commands if those patterns are unexpected; (2) enforce the pre-push git hook (already present per mission context) as a second line of defence — it fires on the git binary itself, not on the calling command string; (3) use `updatedInput` to rewrite `git push --force` → `git push --force-with-lease` as a softer alternative for non-main branches.
- [DENY|both|risk:med|high] The settings.json "denyList" (Bash command patterns at the permissions level) provides a SEPARATE enforcement layer that blocks before hooks run. Deny rules in settings.json cannot carry allow-exceptions and FIRST-MATCH-WINS (deny > ask > allow), but they are simpler string/glob matches without the subcommand-parsing intelligence of hooks. They also lack feedback to Claude about why the command was blocked. => Layer both: put coarse deny rules in settings.json for absolutely-never patterns (e.g., `git push --force` to main) as a fast first gate, then back them with the Node.js PreToolUse hook for nuanced handling, better feedback, and the --no-verify / reset --hard / clean -f cases that are harder to express as glob strings. The hook's permissionDecisionReason is what guides Claude to a safer alternative; the settings.json deny just hard-stops it.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|med] settings.json deny-list glob patterns have the same VAR=/ subcommand parsing semantics as the "if" field when matching Bash tool invocations — and the same fail-open edge: patterns that specify more than the command name run the hook anyway on $(), backticks, or $VAR-expanded fragments. A `Bash(git push --force *)` deny rule will NOT catch `FOO=1 bash -c 'git push --force'` because the outer command is `bash`, not `git`. => Never rely on settings.json deny rules alone for the interpreter-bypass class. The deny list is effective for direct git invocations typed by Claude. Pair it with the Node hook which inspects the full command string including interpreter wrapping (add a pattern: /\b(?:bash|sh|pwsh)\b[^'"]*['"][^'"]*git[^'"]*push[^'"]*--force/ to catch shell-via-interpreter wrapping).
- [ADVISORY|both|risk:none|high] The "if" field has an undocumented asymmetric fail-open specifically for over-specific patterns: "patterns that specify more than the command name always run the hook anyway on $(), backticks, or $VAR". This means `Bash(git push --force)` as an "if" value will fire the hook on ANY command containing $() or backticks, not just push --force commands — creating false-positive spawns (performance issue, not security issue, since the hook script itself does the real check). => For the "if" field used as a spawn filter, keep patterns broad (e.g., `Bash(git *)`) rather than trying to match the exact flag sequence. The overly-specific pattern behavior is documented as intentional: Claude Code prefers over-spawning over under-spawning. Accept this and let the Node.js script do precise matching.
PITFALLS: Using exit 2 as the primary block path silently discards hookSpecificOutput JSON, meaning permissionDecisionReason and additionalContext are never delivered — Claude gets only a generic stderr message and may retry with the same dangerous command. Always use exit 0 + JSON for structured denial. | A hook that exits 1 (conventional Unix error) or crashes with an uncaught exception is FAIL-OPEN — Claude Code proceeds with the tool call as if no hook ran. Wrap all hook logic in try/catch and emit a deny decision in the catch. | jq is NOT guaranteed on Windows and should never be imported as a dependency in hooks. Node.js's built-in JSON.parse is the safe alternative. | The settings.json deny glob `Bash(git push --force *)` does NOT match `git push --force` without a trailing argument (no space after --force). Include both `Bash(git push --force)` and `Bash(git push --force *)` or use the hook approach which handles both via regex. | Compound command VAR= stripping applies only at the TOP LEVEL of the command string. `FOO=1 bash -c 'git push --force'` strips `FOO=1` correctly, but the inner `bash -c 'git push --force'` is then matched against `bash *`, not `git *` — the nested git command is invisible to the deny rule. | The `updatedInput` rewrite approach (--force → --force-with-lease) is elegant but has a correctness trap: --force-with-lease requires the remote tracking ref to be current; on a freshly cloned or rebased branch it may fail differently. Use rewrite only after checking that the branch has a remote tracking ref, or escalate to ask instead. | On Windows with Git Bash in PATH, Claude Code MAY invoke hooks via Git Bash sh.exe rather than cmd.exe depending on runtime. A hook registered as `"command":"node"` bypasses this entirely — this is why the Node.js exec form is strongly preferred over shell form for security gates. | The `if` field is documented as best-effort and the docs themselves say to use the permission system for hard allow/deny — yet the permission system (settings.json) also has the same subcommand-parsing semantics and interpreter-bypass blind spot. Neither layer alone is sufficient; they must be combined with the hook script doing precise string analysis.
OPENQ: Does permissionDecision:"deny" in hookSpecificOutput suppress the tool call silently (no user notification) or does it surface the permissionDecisionReason to the user UI as well as Claude? The docs say it is 'shown to Claude' — unclear if the Ultron/desktop UI also shows it. | When multiple PreToolUse hooks are registered for the same matcher and one returns deny while another returns allow, which wins? The docs mention 'a single deny decision blocks even if other hooks return allow' but this is from a third-party summary, not confirmed verbatim in official docs during this session. | Is there a documented maximum command string length for the hook's stdin JSON? Extremely long commands with embedded here-docs could potentially overflow hook processing in unusual ways. | Can `updatedInput.command` be used to REWRITE a dangerous command to a safer one (e.g., --force → --force-with-lease) while setting permissionDecision:"allow" — or does updatedInput only take effect when the decision is defer/allow? The schema shows both fields simultaneously but the interaction is not confirmed on an official page. | For the Ultron anticheat context: does spawning a Node.js child process for every Bash PreToolUse hook create a detectable process pattern that Vanguard's kernel driver could flag? Node.js is a standard developer tool, but the frequency of spawns during active sessions is unclear.

### PostToolUse format/lint/stub-scan without churn
PostToolUse (Edit|Write|MultiEdit) hooks can deliver maximum quality teeth at near-zero friction when scoped correctly: (1) use `tool_input.file_path` (always present for these three tools) to target the single changed file only — never glob the tree; (2) run `ruff check --no-fix` + `ruff format --check` for check-only lint/format feedback (exit 1 = issues, exit 0 = clean) and return `additionalContext` via `hookSpecificOutput` instead of `decision:"block"` for legacy files with known pre-existing issues; (3) the existing canon ENFORCEMENT.md shell uses `ruff format "$f"` (WRITE mode), which will reformat whole legacy files including unmodified lines — this must be changed to `ruff format --check "$f"` for advisory-only or scoped to new files only; (4) stub-scan with the current `grep -EnI` regex is sound for comment lines but FIX002/FIX001/FIX003/FIX004 (ruff) fire on ANY line containing the keyword including string literals and docstrings — use `grep` in the hook confined to non-test `.py` files for reliable stub detection; (5) on Windows, use Node.js (`readFileSync(0,'utf-8')`) rather than bash+jq because `/dev/stdin` is unavailable; (6) the `hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext` field is nested under `hookSpecificOutput` (not top-level), while `decision:"block"` is top-level — the canon ENFORCEMENT.md example puts `additionalContext` at top-level (wrong); (7) mypy must be scoped to the edited file with `[[tool.mypy.overrides]]` `ignore_errors=true` or `follow_imports=silent` for orchestrator.py to avoid ~10,000 cascading errors on every edit; PGH003 (blanket type:ignore) is NOT enabled by default and is deliberately excluded from new defaults — do not add it globally on a legacy codebase without a per-file-ignores escape hatch.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] PostToolUse fires AFTER the file is already written; exit 2 stops Claude before its next model call but cannot undo the disk write. The PostToolUse JSON output schema is: top-level `decision:"block"` + `reason` to stop the turn, and a NESTED `hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext` / `hookSpecificOutput.updatedToolOutput` for advisory feedback. The canon ENFORCEMENT.md example incorrectly places `additionalContext` at the top level outside `hookSpecificOutput`. => For format/lint feedback that should NOT halt work on legacy files, return `{"hookSpecificOutput":{"hookEventName":"PostToolUse","additionalContext":"ruff: 3 warnings in orchestrator.py (pre-existing, not introduced by this edit)"}}` with exit 0. For a hard block on new stubs or critical violations, use top-level `{"decision":"block","reason":"..."}`. Never use `decision:"block"` for pre-existing violations — this creates confirmation fatigue and will cause the user to disable the hook.
- [HOOK|ultron|risk:high|high] The existing canon ENFORCEMENT.md `post-edit-format-and-stub-scan.sh` runs `ruff format "$f"` (WRITE mode, not check). On a 10,865-line legacy file like orchestrator.py, this will reformat ALL unmodified lines on every edit — violating the surgical-diff requirement and producing noise diffs that confuse git blame, reviewers, and the pre-push hook. => Change `ruff format "$f"` to `ruff format --check "$f"` for check-only mode (exit 1 if file would change, exit 0 if clean). Return the result as `additionalContext` not a block. For NEW files (not in git yet: `git ls-files --error-unmatch "$f" 2>/dev/null || echo new`), auto-fix is acceptable. For files already tracked by git, use check-only. Separately, add `ruff check --no-fix "$f"` for lint violations. Ruff exits 0 = clean, 1 = violations found, 2 = config/internal error.
- [HOOK|ultron|risk:none|high] The `tool_input.file_path` field is present and absolute for all three tools (Edit, Write, MultiEdit). For MultiEdit, the schema is `tool_input.file_path` (single path) + `tool_input.edits[]`. So a single `jq -r '.tool_input.file_path'` correctly scopes all three tools to the one changed file. On Windows, `/dev/stdin` is unavailable — use Node.js `readFileSync(0,'utf-8')` (file descriptor 0 = stdin, cross-platform) or PowerShell `$input = $args[0]; $json = [Console]::In.ReadToEnd() | ConvertFrom-Json`. => Write the PostToolUse hook in Node.js (`.mjs`) invoked as `node .claude/hooks/post-edit-lint.mjs`. This is guaranteed available on Windows (Claude Code requires Node.js). Use `const input = JSON.parse(require('fs').readFileSync(0,'utf-8')); const fp = input.tool_input?.file_path;` to get the file path. Do NOT use `/dev/stdin` or `jq` — both can be absent on Windows. Use `path.join()` not backslash concatenation for any path manipulation.
- [HOOK|both|risk:med|high] Ruff FIX001/FIX002/FIX003/FIX004 rules (FIXME/TODO/XXX/HACK detection) are NOT enabled by default — they require explicit `--select FIX` or config. More critically, these rules fire on ANY line containing the keyword, including string literals, docstrings, and comments-as-data (e.g., regex pattern strings containing the word 'TODO'). This is a known characteristic of pygrep-hooks-style text scanning. In Ultron/Kenning, the corpus includes response text pools that may legitimately contain these words. => For stub-scan, prefer targeted `grep` in the hook script over ruff FIX rules, SPECIFICALLY matching only Python comment syntax: `grep -EnI '^[^#]*#.*\bTODO\b' "$fp"` or the Node.js equivalent using line-by-line parsing. Only flag lines where the keyword appears in a `# comment` (starts with `#` after optional whitespace), not inside strings. Also exclude `# type: ignore` without error codes (PGH003) from global ruff config on the legacy file — it is not in the default ruleset and adding it to orchestrator.py would generate hundreds of suppressions.
- [CONFIG|ultron|risk:high|high] Mypy on a single Python file follows ALL imports by default (`--follow-imports=normal`). Running `mypy src/kenning/pipeline/orchestrator.py` on a 10,865-line untyped legacy file will follow imports into every dependency in the kenning package, potentially generating thousands of errors from unrelated modules. Per mypy docs, `[[tool.mypy.overrides]]` with `module="kenning.pipeline.orchestrator"` and `ignore_errors=true` or `follow_imports="silent"` suppresses errors for that module while keeping strict checks on new files. => Add a mypy override to pyproject.toml silencing orchestrator.py entirely (or using `follow_imports="silent"`) so the PostToolUse hook can safely run `mypy --no-error-summary <file>` on newly edited files without cascading into the legacy monolith. For new files (detected by `git ls-files --error-unmatch` failing), run mypy with `--strict --ignore-missing-imports`. For existing files, run with `--ignore-missing-imports` only. Never run mypy project-wide from a PostToolUse hook — use CI for that.
- [HOOK|both|risk:none|high] The `matcher` field in settings.json for PostToolUse hooks accepts either an exact tool name, a `|`-separated list, or a JavaScript regex (when the string contains characters other than letters/digits/`_`/`|`). The pattern `Edit|Write|MultiEdit` is a valid `|`-separated list (no regex chars) and will match all three file-editing tools. There is also an `if` field for file-pattern sub-filtering using permission rule syntax (`Edit(*.py)`, `Write(src/*)`), distinct from the `matcher` field. => Use `"matcher": "Edit|Write|MultiEdit"` for the PostToolUse hook to catch all file mutations. Add an `if` sub-filter if you want to restrict to Python files only: `"if": "Edit(**/*.py)|Write(**/*.py)"`. This avoids running the ruff/mypy hook on TypeScript, YAML, or shell edits. For the Frontier Kit (language-agnostic), omit the `if` and branch inside the Node.js hook on file extension.
- [HOOK|both|risk:low|high] Advisory `additionalContext` vs hard `decision:"block"` is the critical policy split. `additionalContext` (nested under `hookSpecificOutput`) injects a system reminder into Claude's next model call — Claude sees it and can decide to self-correct, but the turn is NOT blocked and no confirmation fatigue occurs. `decision:"block"` stops execution before the next model call and forces Claude to address it.
