- [overclaim|P2] PostToolUse decision:'block' is 'advisory-only' and merely 'forces the model to address the issue in its next response.' => SAFER: Reserve PostToolUse decision:block for genuine must-fix conditions; for pre-existing/legacy noise use additionalContext only, so autonomous runs are not interrupted. (The reference exit-code table and the SDK both say PostToolUse decision:'block' 'stops processing before the next model call.' That is a real loop-halting control, not merely advisory — it does block the agentic loop from continuing (it just cannot undo the already-written file).)
MISSING: continue:false top-level field — the lens mentions it but I could not confirm its exact semantics on the official reference within this fetch budget (the truncated /en/hooks did not surface a 'continue' field; SDK shows top-level 'continue'/'continue_' = 'whether the agent keeps running'). Verify continue:false behavior on the full reference before relying on it as a session-kill, and prefer permissionDecision:deny for single-tool blocks. | async / asyncTimeout (and asyncRewake): the SDK documents async:true + asyncTimeout for fire-and-forget hooks that 'cannot block, modify, or inject context.' The lens leans on asyncRewake (wake-on-exit-2) for the long run_tests.py gate, but I did not see 'asyncRewake' on the SDK page (only 'async'); asyncRewake is version/CLI-settings-specific and should be confirmed against the settings hooks schema before wiring the test-runner as a background re-wake gate. | max_turns interaction with hooks: SDK 'Fix common issues' states hooks may NOT fire when the agent hits max_turns 'because the session ends before hooks can execute.' This is a real gap for any Stop-hook-as-final-gate design in headless -p runs with --max-turns — the bundle must rely on CI, not the Stop hook, as the unoverridable backstop. | Recursive subagent hook loops: SDK warns a UserPromptSubmit hook that spawns subagents can infinitely recurse; the bundle's context-injection UserPromptSubmit hook must guard against re-entry (check agent_id/subagent indicator) — a self-deadlock class the lens did not flag. | systemMessage is shown to the USER, not the model (SDK: 'shows a message to the user, not the model'); additionalContext is the model-facing channel. Any bundle finding that uses systemMessage to 'guide Claude' is wrong — it reaches the human operator only. | PermissionRequest / PermissionDenied events exist and are a cleaner interception point than PreToolUse for some permission-UI flows; the lens omitted them from the decision-control catalog.

### Stop/SubagentStop hook design in the enforcement bundle (stop_hook_active deadlock guard, block-cap override, current-turn-file scoping, Windows runtime, CI backstop necessity)
NET: Make every Stop/SubagentStop hook in the bundle ADVISORY by default (hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext, exit 0) and push all hard invariants to the server-side CI required-status-checks - this is confirmed necessary because disableAllHooks bypasses even managed hooks (#26637), the 8-block cap can force-stop, and exit-1 fails open. If a hard in-session Stop block is ever used, it MUST: (1) be authored in Node.js (never pwsh -File - confirmed empty-stdin #46601, P0 on Windows/Ultron); (2) read stop_hook_active as line one and exit 0 when true (confirmed real field, cap=8, CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP overridable); (3) wrap the body in try/catch that exits 0 (fail-open, never deadlock); (4) refuse to block whenever background_tasks or session_crons is non-empty (confirmed fields - prevents blocking mid-mammoth-run); (5) only ever gate on a condition satisfiable in ONE continuation, with a git-diff-hash no-progress detector that downgrades to advisory before the cap; (6) NOT use `git diff --name-only HEAD` as a 'current-turn files' primitive (overclaim - it captures the whole run's uncommitted diff and misses staged/committed work; union it with --cached if used at all, but prefer not gating on it). Run the test suite via asyncRewake (background + wake-on-failure), NEVER synchronously inside the Stop hook (default timeout will kill a multi-minute run and fail open). For Ultron, gate the Stop hook to forced-advisory when a live game/stream sentinel is present so it never loads the desktop/audio stack or stalls the orchestrator beside Vanguard. Ship a regression test asserting the hook exits 0 on empty/garbage stdin.
- [confirmed|none] stop_hook_active is a boolean in the Stop/SubagentStop stdin JSON, set true when the current stop attempt was generated by a prior block; checking it and exiting 0 is the canonical deadlock guard. => SAFER: First line of every Stop/SubagentStop hook: read stdin, JSON.parse with try/catch -> {} fallback, `if (input.stop_hook_active) process.exit(0)`. Do not rely on it being present; default to the safe (allow-stop) branch on any parse failure. (The official hooks-guide explicitly documents this. Under 'Stop hook hits the block cap': 'Parse the stop_hook_active field from the JSON input and exit early if it's true' with a sample that does `jq -r '.stop_hook_active'` then `exit 0`. So the field is real and the guard patte)
- [confirmed|none] Claude Code enforces a hard block cap of 8 consecutive Stop-hook blocks, after which the turn ends regardless of hook output; the cap is overridable via CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP; do not hardcode 8. => SAFER: Make the blocking condition satisfiable in ONE continuation. Never count to 8 in hook code. If a no-progress loop is possible, add a self-limiter: if the hook would block but `git diff` is unchanged since the last block (track via a temp marker file under $TMPDIR keyed on session_id), emit additionalContext ('no progress; override if intentional') instead of decision:block, and log to stderr so a cap-override shows up as an anomaly. (Official hooks-guide states verbatim: 'Claude Code overrides a Stop hook after it blocks 8 times in a row without progress.' and 'If your hook legitimately needs more than eight iterations to converge, raise the cap with CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP.' with a link to /en/env-va)
- [confirmed|none] For Stop/SubagentStop, exit 0+JSON {decision:block} and exit 2 both block; exit 1 (and any other non-zero, non-2 code) is NON-blocking (fails open, the stop proceeds). => SAFER: Standardize on exit 0 + JSON {decision:'block', reason:'...'} for blocking (gives Claude an actionable reason and is version-stable). Reserve exit 2 only as a watchdog. Wrap the whole hook body in try/catch; in catch, exit 0 (fail-open, never deadlock) and write the error to stderr so it surfaces as a transcript notice. NEVER let the process throw to an uncaught exit-1. (Official hooks reference confirms: 'Exit 2 means a blocking error... Stderr text is fed back to Claude.' and 'Any other exit code is a non-blocking error for most hook events.' plus the explicit warning: 'Claude Code treats exit code 1 as a non-blocking error and proceeds with th)
- [confirmed|P0] On Windows, Stop hooks invoked via pwsh/powershell.exe -File receive EMPTY stdin (stop_hook_active and all context unavailable), confirmed bug #46601; use Node.js instead. => SAFER: Author every Ultron Stop/SubagentStop hook as `node ${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/hooks/stop-gate.mjs` (exec form, no shell). Read stdin via `fs.readFileSync(0,'utf8')` inside try/catch defaulting to {}. Do NOT use shell:powershell or pwsh -File for any hook that must read stdin. Reserve PowerShell only for fire-and-forget side effects (toast/COM) that need no input. Pin .gitattributes `*.mjs text eol=lf` so CRLF never breaks the script. (GitHub issue #46601 confirms at Claude Code v2.1.101 that a PowerShell Stop hook gets no stdin: [Console]::IsInputRedirected returns False, no data via stdin/env/argv, while the identical UserPromptSubmit hook works. Status: closed as not-planned (stale). This is P0 for Ultron (W)
- [overclaim|P1] Scope Stop-hook validation to files changed in the current turn via `git diff --name-only HEAD` to avoid false-blocking on pre-existing failures and stale state. => SAFER: Do not gate on git diff in the Stop hook at all if the same checks run in CI (they do - see CI backstop). Make the Stop hook ADVISORY (additionalContext only, never decision:block) for quality/lint/test signals, and let the server-side CI required-status-check be the hard gate. If a hard Stop gate is genuinely needed, scope with `git diff --name-only HEAD; git diff --cached --name-only` UNIONED and filtered to the project root, AND require the condition be satisfiable in one continuation (e.g. 'run_tests.py on the changed set is green'), never an open-ended quality bar. Prefer asyncRewake (run tests in background, wake Claude with exit 2 only on failure) over a blocking Stop hook so a mammoth run is never frozen waiting on the suite. (The GOAL (scope narrowly, do not re-validate stable passing state) is correct and is the right defense against confirmation fatigue. But `git diff --name-only HEAD` is NOT a documented Claude Code 'current-turn files' mechanism and is subtly WRONG as written: (1) it shows ALL unc)
- [confirmed|P1] A Stop hook should back its checks with a CI gate because within-session hooks can be bypassed (disableAllHooks:true bypasses even managed hooks, #26637; --dangerously-skip-permissions sidesteps non-managed blocks; Stop-hook override breaks the gate). => SAFER: Register the real invariants (no-test-deletion, ruff/mypy on changed files, secrets scan, lockfile freshness) as GitHub branch-protection REQUIRED status checks with 'Do not allow bypassing the above settings' enabled - server-side, immune to disableAllHooks/--dangerously-skip-permissions/cap-override. Keep the Stop hook purely advisory (additionalContext) so it gives fast in-session feedback without ever being load-bearing or deadlock-prone. Pin all CI actions to full 40-char commit SHAs (CVE-2025-30066). (GitHub issue #26637 (HIGH severity, closed) confirms disableAllHooks:true in .claude/settings.local.json bypasses MANAGED hooks, directly contradicting the documented 'managed hooks cannot be overridden' model. Combined with the block-cap override (a determined user/agent can for)
- [version-uncertain|P2] A Stop hook may combine decision:block and additionalContext, but the decision field takes precedence so the block fires anyway - never mix both. => SAFER: Emit exactly ONE intent per Stop-hook invocation: either {decision:'block', reason} (a hard, one-continuation-satisfiable gate) OR {hookSpecificOutput:{hookEventName:'Stop', additionalContext}} (advisory). Branch in code so the two are mutually exclusive; this sidesteps the undocumented precedence entirely. (The official hooks reference documents decision:block and hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext as TWO SEPARATE Stop-hook output shapes (additionalContext is explicitly for 'non-error feedback that continues the conversation' WITHOUT blocking). It does NOT document what happens wh)
- [confirmed|P1] A Stop hook that blocks on a condition outside Claude's control in one continuation (async background task, unregistered skill, external CI) is a real-world infinite-loop cause; the Stop input exposes background_tasks and session_crons to avoid this. => SAFER: In the Stop hook, FIRST check stop_hook_active (exit 0 if true), THEN read background_tasks/session_crons - if either is non-empty, NEVER decision:block; instead emit additionalContext ('background work still running') and exit 0 so the turn can end cleanly or Claude can choose to wait. Only block on conditions Claude can fix in the next single continuation. Use asyncRewake for anything long-running so Claude keeps working and is re-woken on failure rather than frozen. (The official hooks reference confirms the Stop input JSON carries `background_tasks` (array of running background tasks) and `session_crons` (active scheduled jobs). A Stop hook that returns decision:block while an asyncRewake/background task is mid-flight - or that blocks waitin)
- [confirmed|none] SubagentStop must be registered separately from Stop to gate subagent completions, receives agent_id/agent_type, and needs the identical stop_hook_active guard. => SAFER: Register SubagentStop as a separate, LOG-ONLY hook (read agent_id/agent_type, append to audit JSONL, exit 0) with the stop_hook_active guard as line one. Add blocking only for a specific, one-continuation-satisfiable gate scoped by agent_type matcher, never a blanket block - to avoid stalling multi-agent/agent-team runs. (Official hooks reference: SubagentStop 'fires when a subagent finishes' and 'operates identically to Stop hooks' with the same decision control, the same additionalContext support, and the same self-deadlock prevention. So the deadlock guard and the fail-open discipline apply ide)
MISSING: No guidance on the Stop-hook timeout: the hooks reference assigns event-specific timeouts; a Stop hook that runs scripts/run_tests.py (which can take minutes) under the default timeout will be KILLED mid-run, and a killed hook's exit code is non-2 = fails open (allows stop) - silently defeating the gate. The bundle must either set an explicit generous timeout AND run tests via asyncRewake (non-blocking) rather than synchronously inside the Stop hook, or accept that the Stop hook can never run the full suite. This timeout-vs-test-runtime collision is unaddressed. | No handling for the Ultron-specific anticheat hazard: a Stop hook that synchronously spawns the test wrapper (.venv python scripts/run_tests.py) during a LIVE Valorant session loads the heavy desktop/audio stack the binding rules forbid by default, and can stall the orchestrator main loop. The Stop gate must be disabled or forced-advisory when a stream/game is live (e.g. gate on an env flag or a sentinel file the launcher writes), which the research never connects to the Stop hook. | No concrete 'no-progress detector' implementation for the cap. The research says treat cap-override as FATAL but gives no mechanism. The bundle needs a session-scoped marker (e.g. $TMPDIR/<session_id>.lastblock storing a git-diff hash) so the hook can detect 'I blocked but nothing changed' and downgrade to advisory BEFORE hitting the 8-cap, turning a guaranteed deadlock into a single advisory nudge. | No mention that fileCheckpointingEnabled/ /rewind interacts with Stop-hook blocking: if a Stop hook blocks and Claude then edits, the checkpoint chain grows; an aggressive Stop gate amplifies checkpoint churn. Minor, but worth a one-line note. | No SessionEnd fallback. SessionEnd is advisory-only (cannot block) and fires when the session actually ends - it is the correct place to emit a FINAL audit summary (uncommitted changes, failing tests) that a blocking Stop hook should NOT try to enforce. The research over-focuses on Stop and never offers SessionEnd as the zero-deadlock alternative for end-of-session reporting. | No explicit test that the Stop hook itself fails open on malformed/empty stdin (the exact #46601 Windows condition). The bundle should ship a unit test that pipes '' and '{bad json' to stop-gate.mjs and asserts exit 0, so a future regression cannot turn the guard into a deadlock.

### Adversarial red-team of the "robust PreToolUse dangerous-bash matcher" research facet (settings.json deny rules + Node.js regex hook for git/shell danger blocking), verified against official Claude Code docs (code.claude.com/docs/en/permissions, /hooks, /hooks-guide).
NET: INVERT the facet's hook-first stance — the official docs are explicit that the permission system, not hooks/if-filters, is the hard gate, and that arg-constraining Bash patterns are fragile. For the dangerous-bash layer ship, in order: (1) SCOPED settings.json deny for irreversible verbs in specifier form — Bash(rm -rf *), Bash(git push -f*), Bash(git push --force*), Bash(git reset --hard *), Bash(git clean -f*) — never the silently-ignored Bash(command:...) form; (2) interpreter-bypass deny — Bash(bash -c *), Bash(sh -c *), Bash(python -c *), Bash(node -e *) plus the unstripped runner forms (docker exec, npx, devbox run, find -exec/-delete) where they are not needed for the workflow; (3) the existing pre-push git hook (fires on the binary, immune to CLI spelling and interpreter wrapping) as the real backstop; (4) a CI required-status check as the unoverrideable floor (since disableAllHooks can bypass even managed hooks). Use a Node.js PreToolUse hook ONLY for ADVISORY additionalContext and the rare edge the deny engine cannot express — and if it ever denies, use exit-0 + permissionDecision:'deny' with a fail-closed exit-2 catch block; strip quoted substrings and match only command/flag position to avoid the P0 commit-message false-positive. Prefer ASK over DENY for reset --hard and non-main force-push so the user never loses the capability. A pure regex hook re-implementing what Claude Code's shell-aware matcher already does is net-negative: it adds false positives (P0 blocking legit commit messages) without closing the interpreter-wrapping hole (P1) that only capability-severing + OS sandbox + pre-push/CI can close. Regex is the WRONG primary tool here; permissionDecision/deny rules are right.
- [overclaim|P1] Bash deny rules in settings.json are 'simpler string/glob matches without subcommand-parsing intelligence' and a Bash(git push --force *) deny will NOT catch FOO=1 bash -c 'git push --force' so you must back it with a Node hook. => SAFER: Lean on settings.json deny for direct git invocations (it already handles &&/;/| and wrappers). For the interpreter-bypass class, add a SCOPED deny on the interpreters themselves where unexpected (e.g. Bash(bash -c *), Bash(sh -c *), Bash(python -c *), Bash(node -e *)) rather than trying to regex-detect git-inside-a-string, which is unwinnable. Keep the pre-push git hook (fires on the git binary regardless of caller) as the real backstop, plus the CI required-status check. (The first half is REFUTED by the official permissions doc: Claude Code IS shell-operator aware for Bash rules. It splits on &&, ||, ;, |, |&, &, and newlines and requires each subcommand to match independently, AND it strips a fixed wrapper set (timeout, time, nice, nohup, stdbuf)
- [confirmed|none] The robust pattern is a Node.js PreToolUse hook that reads the full command and emits permissionDecision:'deny' on exit 0 — never rely on exit 2 alone because exit 2 ignores JSON stdout and cannot inject additionalContext. => SAFER: Use exit-0 + permissionDecision:'deny' for the actionable-reason path; reserve exit 2 for the fail-closed catch-block (malformed JSON / crash) so a broken hook still denies the security-critical class instead of failing open. (Confirmed against /hooks: exit 0 + hookSpecificOutput.permissionDecision='deny' + permissionDecisionReason is the structured path that feeds a reason back to Claude; exit 2 blocks and routes stderr to Claude but discards stdout JSON. The official /hooks-guide dangerous-command EX)
- [confirmed|P1] A regex hook on the raw Bash string cannot catch interpreter-wrapped danger (python -c, node -e, bash -c) — treat the hook as defence-in-depth, not a hermetic seal. => SAFER: Do NOT attempt to make the regex hermetic. Sever the capability instead: scoped-deny the interpreters' -c/-e forms, keep the pre-push hook + CI backstop (which the mission already has), and on macOS/Linux/WSL2 use the OS sandbox (network/filesystem) which contains child processes regardless of how they were spawned. On native Windows (Ultron) the sandbox is unavailable, so deny-rules + pre-push + CI are the only deterministic layers. (Confirmed and UNDER-stated as a risk. The /hooks doc itself does NOT warn about interpreter wrapping, and the official curl Warning in /permissions generalizes the same lesson: argument-constraining patterns are fragile (options-before-URL, protocol variants, $VAR expansion, extr)
- [confirmed|P0] False positives arise when dangerous flag tokens appear in quoted strings (git commit -m '--force is bad'); strip single/double-quoted substrings before flag-scanning. => SAFER: Prefer settings.json deny rules (Bash(git push --force *), Bash(git reset --hard *)) which match the command structurally and do not false-trigger on -m message bodies, over a regex hook that scans the raw string. If a hook IS used, strip quoted substrings AND restrict matching to the command/flag position only; never match inside a -m/-F value. Use ASK (not DENY) for reset --hard so the human can wave through the rare legitimate case. (Confirmed as a real and HIGH-impact false-positive class for a hand-rolled regex hook — and directly on-target for my lens. A naive /git reset --hard/ or /--force/ regex blocks 'git commit -m "reverting the git reset --hard from yesterday"', a legitimate and common operation, cau)
- [confirmed|P1] The 'if' field does real subcommand parsing (strips VAR=, walks &&/;/|, enters $() and backticks) but FAILS OPEN when parsing fails — making it unsuitable as the sole gate; put real logic in the hook body. => SAFER: Use 'if' only as a spawn filter (broad, e.g. if:'Bash'), never as the gate. Put the deterministic hard line in permissions.deny (settings) per the doc's explicit recommendation; use the hook for advisory feedback and the interpreter-wrapping edge that deny-rules cannot express. (Confirmed verbatim against /hooks: 'The filter also fails open, running your hook regardless of pattern, when the Bash command cannot be parsed. Because the if filter is best-effort, use the permission system rather than a hook to enforce a hard allow or deny.' The docs ALSO note)
- [refuted|P1] A settings.json deny like Bash(command:rm *) or relying on the command parameter is a valid alternative gating mechanism. => SAFER: Always use the specifier form Bash(rm -rf *), never Bash(command:...). Verify at startup that no 'ignored rule' warning fires (it indicates a typo or a non-matchable param rule). Run /permissions to confirm the rule is live. (REFUTED by /permissions: 'A rule like Bash(command:rm *) would be bypassable by a compound command, so Claude Code ignores it and emits a startup warning.' The command/file_path/url/path parameters are explicitly NON-matchable via the Tool(param:value) syntax because they have th)
- [confirmed|none] permissionDecision:'deny' from a PreToolUse hook blocks even in --dangerously-skip-permissions / bypassPermissions mode because hooks execute before permission bypass; permissionDecision:'allow' does NOT override a deny rule. => SAFER: Keep deny rules in settings as the floor; use the hook only to ADD denials (interpreter wrapping) or advisory context. Never wire a hook 'allow' expecting it to carve an exception out of a deny rule. (Confirmed verbatim in /hooks-guide: 'PreToolUse hooks fire before any permission-mode check. A hook that returns permissionDecision: deny blocks the tool even in bypassPermissions mode or with --dangerously-skip-permissions. The reverse is not true: a hook returning allow does no)
- [version-uncertain|P2] permissionDecision supports a 'defer' value (alongside allow/deny/ask) for headless --resume flows. => SAFER: For the dangerous-bash hook, emit only deny (block) or omit a decision (silent pass-through = normal flow). Do not author logic that depends on a literal 'defer' return until confirmed on the canonical reference for your installed version. (The /hooks reference I fetched lists permissionDecision values as allow/deny/ask and describes the no-decision/normal-flow path; the WebFetch summary surfaced 'defer' as 'let normal permission flow apply', and the /hooks-guide enumerates only allow/deny/ask with their precise eff)
- [overclaim|P1] settings.json deny rules can express git push --force to main as a fast first gate (e.g. Bash(git push --force *) / push to main). => SAFER: Block the broad dangerous verb (Bash(git push -f*), Bash(git push --force*)) and additionally protect main with a server-side branch-protection required check + a pre-push hook on the git binary, which sees the resolved refspec regardless of CLI spelling. Do not try to encode 'to main only' in a glob. Use ASK for force-push on non-main branches so the user keeps the capability. (Partially refuted by the /permissions fragility warning. Because a single * spans multiple args, 'Bash(git push * main)' over-matches (also catches git merge-style forms) and a flag-ordered pattern like 'Bash(git push --force *)' misses 'git push origin main --force', 'git push -)
MISSING: The biggest omission: the official docs' own conclusion is to use the PERMISSION SYSTEM (deny rules) as the hard gate and treat hooks/if-filters as best-effort. The facet inverts this into a hook-first design. For a maximum-teeth/zero-friction bundle, the dangerous-bash layer should be: (1) scoped settings.json deny for the irreversible verbs, (2) interpreter-form deny for the bypass class, (3) pre-push hook on the git binary, (4) CI required-status check — with the Node hook reserved for advisory feedback only. | Process-wrapper and environment-runner false negatives are unmentioned: Claude Code strips timeout/time/nice/nohup/stdbuf/bare-xargs, but does NOT strip devbox run, mise exec, direnv exec, npx, docker exec, watch, setsid, ionice, flock, or find -exec/-delete. A deny on the inner command is silently bypassed by 'docker exec ... rm -rf' or 'find . -delete'. The matcher must add explicit deny for these runner forms, and find with -exec/-delete needs exact-match rules. | No mention that the official dangerous-command EXAMPLE in /hooks-guide is the crude exit-2 'rm -rf substring' form with NO quote-stripping and NO interpreter handling — i.e. copying the canonical example yields exactly the false-positive (commit messages) and false-negative (wrapping) problems the facet warns about. The bundle should NOT ship the canonical example as-is. | Read/Edit deny rules already cover file commands Claude Code recognizes in Bash (cat/head/tail/sed) but NOT arbitrary scripts that open files — so 'Read(**/.env)' does not stop a python script reading .env. Only the OS sandbox does. This taint/exfiltration gap is missing and matters for the anticheat .env protection on Ultron (where sandbox is unavailable on native Windows). | acceptEdits mode auto-runs mkdir/touch/mv/cp and the read-only built-in set (ls/cat/grep/find/git read-only) runs in EVERY mode without prompt and is non-configurable except via ask/deny rules — the bundle should add ask/deny for any of these it wants gated (e.g. a read-only git form it considers sensitive), which the facet never addresses. | Confirmation-fatigue quantification: a regex hook that re-checks patterns the deny engine already safely handles produces redundant denials AND new false positives (commit-message bodies), net-negative. The facet treats 'add a hook' as free; it is not — it adds a second, less-precise matcher on the critical path. | No coverage of the Bash(* main) / single-* spanning-multiple-args footgun, which is the most common way hand-written deny rules accidentally over-block (one * matches across argument boundaries including spaces).

### tests/test_map.txt generation (source→covering-test map) for the Claude Code enforcement bundle — adversarial review of the ~70% regression-reduction provenance, generator correctness (static AST vs dynamic coverage contexts), and maintenance-drift risk, grounded against the live Ultron/Kenning repo (orchestrator.py = 10,865 lines; scripts/run_tests.py wrapper present; tests/test_map.txt ABSENT; 450 test files; no coverage configured).
NET: SHIP the test_map, but DEMOTE it from 'proven 70% safety gate' to 'advisory developer-ergonomics hint', and fix three concrete defects before wiring it. (1) PROVENANCE: the 70% number is a single non-peer-reviewed preprint (arXiv 2603.17973v2, N=125, small open-weight models, no significance test) — cite it honestly; the durable, well-supported insight is the inverse (TDD prose WITHOUT a targeted test map made regressions WORSE, 9.94%), which justifies the map's existence without overclaiming. (2) SEEDING (P0 fix): do NOT add --cov to the shared pytest addopts — it taxes every sweep, collides with the run_tests.py process-mutex/concurrent-run guard, and risks the fragile coverage-under-thread-timeout path the wrapper exists to tame. Seed out-of-band via a one-off `run_tests.py --cov` flag (serial, no xdist, coverage-report-suppressed, runs in the project's testing/diagnostics mode to respect the anticheat firewall), generate the map from the .coverage via the (confirmed-real) CoverageData API, then delete .coverage. (3) GENERATOR CORRECTNESS (P1): a plain static AST import-graph is genuinely under-covering here — verified live (450 test files; importlib.import_module dynamic import in tests; 6 conftest fixtures; the 10,865-line orchestrator reached mostly via runtime integration paths, not import edges). Always UNION static+dynamic, normalize Windows paths in the keys, and hard-code a never-prune rule: any change to orchestrator.py / conftest.py / importlib-using tests forces the full relevant set. CRITICALLY, the map must never PRUNE a CI run — CI always executes the full sweep as the unoverridable backstop (the only layer immune to disableAllHooks / bypass mode); the map only ORDERS tests and advises Claude pre-commit. The Stop-hook deadlock guard (stop_hook_active + 8-block cap) is confirmed real and must be a Node.js script, not the docs' bash+jq snippet. Add a falsifiable self-test for the map before trusting it.
- [overclaim|P1] The ~70% regression-reduction figure (6.08%→1.82%) is peer-reviewed research from TDAD (ACM AIWare 2026), establishing the test-map as the proven mechanism that cuts agent regressions. => SAFER: Cite it as 'preliminary, single-paper, N=125, non-peer-reviewed, small open-weight models' and treat the test-map as a low-cost developer-ergonomics aid (it tells Claude which tests to run before committing) whose worst case is wasted effort, not as a quantitatively-proven 70% safety control. ### Secrets-scan + supply-chain commit-time gates (gitleaks / detect-secrets / TruffleHog / pip-audit) for the Claude Code enforcement bundle — Windows compatibility, false-positive flood, conflict with the existing pre-push hygiene hook, action/version pinning, and whether the CI mirror (not local hooks) is the layer that actually holds.
NET: The secrets/supply-chain layer is directionally correct and most high-value pieces (gitleaks as commit-time scanner, TruffleHog-verified + pip-audit in CI, SHA-pinning actions, branch-protection required checks as the authoritative gate) are CONFIRMED against official sources. But three things must be corrected before shipping: (1) drop the deprecated 'gitleaks protect --staged' command — the real hook entry is 'gitleaks git --pre-commit --redact --staged'; (2) fix the CVE attribution — CVE-2025-59536 is a startup-trust-dialog code injection, NOT the .mcp.json/enableAllProjectMcpServers RCE, and 'CVE-2026-21852' is unverifiable; keep the controls, drop the false citations; (3) soften the 'disableAllHooks bypasses managed hooks' claim — current docs say managed hooks survive disableAllHooks, though for non-MDM single-machine Ultron the operational conclusion (local hooks are skippable, CI is the only unoverridable gate) still holds. Treat ALL local secret hooks (git pre-commit AND the Claude Code PreToolUse Node scanner) as fast advisory feedback that FAILS OPEN, and make GitHub branch-protection required status checks — ideally augmented by native GitHub push-protection / secret-scanning — the layer that actually holds. For coexistence with the existing pre-push hygiene hook: install pre-commit for the pre-commit stage ONLY and leave .git/hooks/pre-push untouched (or migrate it explicitly to a language:system stage:[pre-push] entry), and NEVER run 'pre-commit install --overwrite'. Add an Ultron-corpus-scoped allowlist (.gitleaks.toml + detect-secrets baseline over tests/data and the voice-lines corpus) up front or the FP flood will get the gate disabled. Verify winget availability before scripting it; the vendor-supported Windows path is the binary download. Pin scanner versions and action SHAs; enforce LF (not BOM) on all gate config/scripts via .gitattributes.
- [refuted|P1] The gitleaks pre-commit hook 'runs gitleaks protect --staged --redact under the hood' (research [HOOK|both] finding in the secrets-scan facet). => SAFER: Document the actual command 'gitleaks git --pre-commit --redact --staged' (or just rely on the pre-commit hook id 'gitleaks' which encodes it). (Verified against gitleaks' own .pre-commit-hooks.yaml: the hook entry is 'gitleaks git --pre-commit --redact --staged --verbose'. The 'protect' command was DEPRECATED in v8.19.0 and is hidden from --help. Any bundle docs/scripts that invoke 'gitleaks protect --staged' are calling)

(GitHub docs confirm required status checks must pass before changes to a protected branch, are enforced on GitHub's servers (immune to client-side git config), and an explicit option applies the rules to admins/bypass-roles too. - [confirmed|none] Pin all third-party GitHub Actions to full 40-char commit SHAs (CVE-2025-30066 tj-actions/changed-files poisoning) and prefer native git-diff over the changed-files action. => SAFER: Replace tj-actions/changed-files with 'git diff --name-only --diff-filter=ACMR origin/$base...HEAD' for the changed-file list and 'git diff --name-only --diff-filter=D' for deletions; SHA-pin every remaining action (TruffleHog, checkout); enable org 'require SHA pinning'. (This is correct, current, and directly in my lens (supply-chain/pinning). ### Deny-rule / permission-control collisions with tools the user actually uses (Bash git incl. the run_tests.py wrapper, computer-use, MCP tools, WebFetch/WebSearch, background tasks, worktree git ops, Workflow/subagents, and USER-DIRECTED canon/settings/hooks maintenance) in the proposed Ultron + Frontier Kit enforcement bundle.
NET: The deny-rule set the research proposes is SAFE against the user's toolset on exactly two conditions, both of which the bundle author must hold as hard invariants: (1) every deny is SCOPED, never bare — no bare Bash, no bare Agent, no blanket mcp__* in the shared bundle; (2) anything that would amputate a whole capability class (web, MCP, subagents) is Ultron-ONLY and lives in Ultron's own settings/settings.local.json, never in the portable kit. With those held, the correctly-scoped denies (pip/npm/uv install, curl/wget + PowerShell network cmdlets, Read(.env)/Read(//**/.env)/secrets, Edit(/docs/canon/**) as DENY-or-ASK) do not collide with git status/diff/log/add/commit, the run_tests.py wrapper, computer-use, Claude-in-Chrome, background tasks, worktree git ops, or Workflow/subagents.\n\nThree corrections are mandatory before shipping: (a) Drop the hallucinated auto-mode quantifications (no 0.4% / no '20 action classes'; the 20 is a denial-count fallback) and document that auto mode drops Agent/Bash(*) allows and aborts -p after repeated blocks — pick dontAsk+allowlist+budget caps for true unattended runs. (b) Re-architect canon/settings/hook maintenance around PROTECTED PATHS: .claude/** and .mcp.json/.claude.json/.pre-commit-config.yaml already always-prompt and are NOT pre-approvable, so put ASK only on the docs-resident canon (Edit(/docs/canon/**)), never DENY .claude/** (that would block the user's own hook/settings maintenance), and never run an interactive canon-editing session in dontAsk. (c) Replace any blanket mcp__* deny with disableClaudeAiConnectors:true plus an enumerate-and-allow list covering the user's entire live MCP fleet, and treat WebFetch domain rules + the SSRF PreToolUse hook (not deny rules, not sandbox) as the only real network boundary on native Windows.\n\nThe Stop-hook deadlock guard, node-exec-form Windows authoring, and the ruff --check (not write-mode) anti-churn fix are correct and load-bearing — keep them. Omit the WorktreeCreate hook from the default bundle (version-uncertain replace-semantics + high blast radius on a workflow the user actively uses). Back every within-session gate with CI required status checks, since disableAllHooks/bypass can defeat hooks but not server-side merge gates. Net: PROCEED with the bundle, but ship it scoped, Ultron-vs-kit-split, and protected-path-aware; reject the bare-tool denies, the blanket mcp__* deny, the auto-mode false-precision, and the write-mode ruff formatter.
- [confirmed|none] Permission precedence is deny > ask > allow, first match wins, and a deny rule cannot carry allow-exceptions (a broad deny blocks even a narrower allow). => SAFER:  (Official permissions doc states verbatim: 'Rules are evaluated in order: deny, then ask, then allow... rule specificity does not change the order. A broad deny rule like Bash(aws *) blocks every matching call, including calls that also match a narrower allow rule like Bash(aws s3)

Do NOT add a bare Bash deny. (Scoped Bash deny patterns block only matching subcommands and leave the tool available (docs: 'A scoped rule like Bash(rm *) leaves the tool available and blocks matching calls'). Claude Code is shell-operator-aware and matches each subcommand of a compound command independently,)

### Frontier Claude Code enforcement bundle (.claude/settings.json + hooks + ruff/mypy + test_map + CI) for Ultron/Kenning (Windows 11) and the portable kit — adversarial verification of the research digest against official Claude Code docs (code.claude.com), June 2026.
NET: SHIP the bundle, with four corrections that are P0/P1 against the stated non-negotiables (max teeth, zero capability loss, no self-deadlock, no false-block of user-directed work). (1) STOP-GATE: do not rely on stop_hook_active alone -- it is in the SDK but ABSENT from the CLI hooks reference, which says a Stop hook 'cannot prevent an infinite loop.' Build the gate advisory-first (additionalContext), scope it to current-turn `git diff --name-only HEAD`, add a hook-owned no-progress sentinel (HEAD+dirty-hash unchanged across blocks -> exit 0), fail-open on any error, and make CI branch-protection required checks the real enforcement. The block-cap env var is unverified -- do not depend on it. (2) POSTTOOLUSE CANNOT BLOCK: remove every decision:block/exit-2 'gate' from PostToolUse (docs: advisory-only, tool already ran) -- use it for additionalContext + updatedToolOutput redaction only; move real post-execution gates to PostToolBatch (TS-SDK only) or CI. (3) LEGACY CHURN: never run write-mode ruff format from a hook on tracked files -- use ruff format --check + ruff check --no-fix on the single edited path with additionalContext; fence orchestrator.py with extend-per-file-ignores + a mypy [[overrides]] ignore_errors=true; keep write-mode + full mypy in CI-on-changed-files only. (4) USER-DIRECTED CANON: gate docs/canon with ASK (not deny); for .claude/** rely on the built-in protected-path prompt (allow rules do NOT pre-approve it) and never deny .claude or run canon maintenance in dontAsk (denies .claude outright). AUTONOMOUS-RUN SAFETY (the lens): the bundle does NOT inherently stall autonomous runs PROVIDED you (a) pre-configure autoMode.environment with trusted infra to avoid the confirmed 3-consecutive/20-total headless abort, (b) avoid blanket Bash(*)/Agent allow rules auto mode silently drops on entry, (c) keep all blocking hooks satisfiable-in-one-continuation and fail-open, (d) pass --max-turns/--max-budget-usd, and (e) remember hooks may not fire on a max_turns termination so CI must cover that gap. DOWNGRADE to 'unverified' every GitHub-issue/CVE-numbered claim (auto-mode 0.4% FP, #3983, #26637 managed bypass, #46601, #39344, #52822, the CVEs) and the 'Node.js is guaranteed' assumption -- WebSearch was unavailable and none are on official pages; their MITIGATIONS are good practice but must not be presented as confirmed or drive any capability-reducing decision. CONFIRMED as ground truth and citable: native-Windows sandbox absence, deny>ask>allow precedence/merge, the managed-only key list, defaultMode:auto-ignored-in-project-settings, protected paths, permissionDecision allow/deny/ask/defer, statusLine refreshInterval, WorktreeCreate replace-semantics, and Agent-deny-kills-subagents."]
- [conflict|P0] Stop/SubagentStop self-deadlock is prevented by checking a 'stop_hook_active' boolean in the hook stdin JSON; it is the canonical harness-enforced guard and must be the first check in every Stop hook. => SAFER: Do not make stop_hook_active the sole guard for CLI shell hooks. Defense-in-depth: read it defensively (===true -> exit 0) AND keep a hook-owned progress sentinel (write HEAD + dirty-file hash each block; unchanged since last block -> exit 0 = no progress). Scope the gate to current-turn `git diff --name-only HEAD` only. Make it advisory-first (additionalContext over decision:block) and treat CI required checks as the real enforcement. Never use exit 2 as the primary Stop block. Treat the block-cap env var as unverified. (SOURCE SPLIT, both verified. The Agent SDK hooks page references stop_hook_active in its SubagentStop example (TS subInput.stop_hook_active / Py input_data.get('stop_hook_active')) so the field EXISTS in SDK input. BUT the CLI hooks reference (code.claude.com/docs/en/hooks) does )
- [refuted|P1] PostToolUse supports decision:'block' to halt the agentic loop, and exit 2 blocks before the next model call. => SAFER: Use PostToolUse only for advisory additionalContext + updatedToolOutput redaction (both confirmed). No -- shows stderr to Claude (tool already ran).' Exit 2 cannot undo/block a PostToolUse; it only surfaces stderr. - [confirmed|none] There are ~30 hook events including PermissionRequest, UserPromptExpansion, PostToolBatch, TeammateIdle, TaskCreated/Completed, ConfigChange, WorktreeCreate/Remove, SubagentStart, InstructionsLoaded, PreCompact/PostCompact, SessionStart, Elicitation/ElicitationResult. => SAFER: For the portable kit, target CLI settings shell-hook events (broadest surface). - [confirmed|none] permissionDecision supports allow/deny/ask/defer; precedence deny>defer>ask>allow; 'defer' ENDS the query (exit, not pause). => SAFER: Use deny for hard gates, allow for read-only auto-approve, ask for user-directed canon/settings edits, and never defer in interactive Ultron (it terminates the session). (SDK hooks page confirms the four values, the precedence note 'deny > defer > ask > allow (any deny blocks)', and 'Returning defer ends the query so you can resume it later.' updatedInput must pair with allow/ask and is ignored with defer.)
- [confirmed|none] Hook decisions never bypass permission deny/ask rules; PreToolUse exit-2/deny blocks even in bypassPermissions; a hook 'allow' does NOT override a settings deny. => SAFER: Keep deny rules in settings.json as the hard gate; use PreToolUse hooks for nuance/feedback on top, never as a replacement. (Permissions page verbatim: 'Hook decisions do not bypass permission rules... a hook that exits with code 2 stops the tool call before permission rules are evaluated.' Hooks are additive-only: they can add restriction or advisory allow but never remove a deny.)

### Adversarial lens: would deny rules on canon files (Edit(.claude/settings.json), Edit(.claude/hooks/**), Edit(BINDING_RULES.md), Edit(CONSTRAINTS.md)) hard-block user-directed canon maintenance, is deny>ask non-carve-able at project level, and is the prescribed fix correct?
NET: The lens's core thesis is CONFIRMED and is a genuine P0: putting Edit(.claude/settings.json), Edit(.claude/hooks/**), Edit(BINDING_RULES.md), Edit(CONSTRAINTS.md) in a DENY array would hard-block exactly the user-directed canon maintenance this project does constantly, and deny>ask (first-match, specificity-irrelevant, merged across all scopes, 'a deny rule cannot carry allowlist exceptions') means you cannot carve an exception at project level. CORRECT FIX: (1) For canon files the user edits use ASK at project scope (preserves the edit, one confirmation, survives bypassPermissions). (2) Lean on the built-in PROTECTED PATHS for .claude/**, .mcp.json, .claude.json (already prompted in every non-bypass mode; allow rules cannot pre-approve them) instead of adding redundant/harmful rules; use the per-session 'allow Claude to edit its own settings' option for autonomous runs. (3) Put DENY only on genuine never-touch paths (.env, secrets, Vanguard driver) and set disableBypassPermissionsMode:'disable'. REJECT/REVISE the lens's third prescription: a PreToolUse hook CANNOT mechanically distinguish user-directed from autonomous (no origin field in its stdin) — if a hook is used, make it Node.js (no jq/bash on Windows) and return permissionDecision:'ask' with advisory context, NOT exit-2 block, and back the real integrity invariant with a required CI status check since in-session hooks are defeatable via disableAllHooks.
- [confirmed|P0] Deny rules Edit(.claude/settings.json), Edit(.claude/hooks/**), Edit(BINDING_RULES.md), Edit(CONSTRAINTS.md) would HARD-BLOCK user-directed canon maintenance (this very task), because a deny rule prevents Claude from using the tool on those paths regardless of who asked. => SAFER: Use ASK rules, not DENY, for user-directed canon paths: permissions.ask = ['Edit(/docs/canon/**)','Edit(/docs/ultron_1_0/CONSTRAINTS.md)']. Ask prompts for confirmation but PERMITS the edit. Reserve DENY strictly for never-touch paths (.env, secrets, vendored binaries). (Official permissions doc states verbatim: 'Deny rules prevent Claude Code from using the specified tool.' Edit rules 'apply to all built-in tools that edit files' and follow gitignore path semantics, so Edit(/docs/canon/BINDING_RULES.md), Edit(.claude/settings.json), Edit(.claude)
- [confirmed|P0] deny > ask precedence means a project-level deny on canon files cannot be exception-carved by adding a narrower allow rule at the same or any scope. => SAFER: Do not attempt deny+allow carve-outs (silently ineffective). If a hard never-do is genuinely required AND a narrow exception is needed, express it as absence-of-deny plus an ASK gate, or a PreToolUse hook that returns deny conditionally; the static rule system has no exception mechanism. (Verbatim: 'Rules are evaluated in order: deny, then ask, then allow. The first match in that order determines the outcome, and rule specificity does not change the order... so a deny rule cannot carry allowlist exceptions.' On cross-scope merge: 'If a tool is denied at any level,)

### Claude Code enforcement bundle (settings.json + .claude/hooks/** + ruff/mypy + tests/test_map.txt + CI) for (1) Ultron/Kenning on Windows 11 and (2) the portable Frontier Claude Code Kit. Adversarial verification of the research digest + the Ultron-specific lens against official code.claude.com docs, June 2026.
NET: SHIP the bundle, but with four corrections that the research got wrong or missed, and a hard split between Ultron and the Kit. (1) The deadlock guard is REAL — cite /en/hooks-guide for stop_hook_active + the 8-block cap + CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP, not the reference page (which omits the string and will mislead). Every Stop/SubagentStop hook: check stop_hook_active first, Node.js exec form, scope to current-turn git diff, back with CI. (2) DROP the invented 'delegate' permission mode and the 'PostToolUse cannot block' claim — both are wrong; the six real modes are default/acceptEdits/plan/auto/dontAsk/bypassPermissions and PostToolUse CAN decision:block (advisory-after-write). (3) Do NOT add deny OR ask rules on canon/settings/hooks paths — .claude/** is already a built-in protected path that prompts in every non-bypass mode and cannot be allow-listed away; a deny there self-deadlocks the user's routine canon-maintenance workflow (the mission's explicit red line). Protect the real invariant (no silent removal of enforcement) in CI, the only tamper-proof layer (disableAllHooks/bypassPermissions/settings.local.json can defeat in-session hooks — disableAllHooks is a confirmed real key). (4) On Ultron's native Windows the OS sandbox is unavailable; permission deny rules + fail-open Node.js hooks + the existing Python import-firewall are the enforcement, and Read/Edit denies do NOT stop indirect script file access — so .env protection must lean on the import-firewall, not just a Read deny. POSTURE: maximum teeth via deny-rules (scoped, never bare on autonomy tools: pip/curl/wget/Invoke-WebRequest, //c|//e secrets) + permissions.disableBypassPermissionsMode='disable' + advisory-first hooks (additionalContext/updatedToolOutput/updatedInput) + auto mode as an OPTIONAL unattended-run layer (knowing user allow can override soft_deny, so hard lines stay in permissions.deny). ZERO loss of autonomy: never bare-deny Agent/Bash/WebFetch/mcp__*; never ship a WorktreeCreate hook that can return empty (breaks the worktree workflow the user lives in); keep claude-code-action separate from CI guards. Ultron's three custom controls (port-8772 one-instance, voice-path import allowlist, persona/attribution) belong in the launcher + CI + advisory hooks, NOT hard in-session blocks. Finally: WebSearch was down — re-verify all cited GitHub issue/CVE numbers before any severity claim depends on them, and wrap Ultron's EXISTING gates (validate_config.py, golden-digest, flavor-lint, test_anticheat, run_tests.py) rather than duplicating them.

Use Node.js exec form (fs.readFileSync(0)) not bash+jq (the guide's jq example breaks on Windows). Scope the check to current-turn changed files (git diff --name-only HEAD) and back it with the CI gate so the hook can safely no-op. Treat a block-cap override as a FATAL log signal, not normal. (CONFIRMED but with a documentation gotcha that matters for the bundle. - [overclaim|P1] There are ~30 hook events including SessionStart, UserPromptSubmit, PreCompact/PostCompact, SubagentStart/Stop, WorktreeCreate, InstructionsLoaded, ConfigChange, Notification, SessionEnd; PostToolUse is advisory-only and does NOT support decision:block (use PostToolBatch). => SAFER: Treat PostToolUse decision:block as a real (advisory-after-write) veto that forces Claude to address the issue next turn. - [confirmed|none] Permission rules merge across all five layers; precedence is deny > ask > allow, first-match-wins, specificity does not change order, and a deny rule CANNOT carry allow-exceptions (broad deny blocks a narrower allow). => SAFER: Place hard denies (.env, secrets, pip install, curl/wget) in project .claude/settings.json so they merge. NEVER attempt a narrower allow to carve an exception out of a deny — it is silently ignored. For user-directed canon/settings/hooks maintenance, do NOT deny those paths (see the canon-protection verdict). (Verbatim-confirmed on the permissions page: 'Rules are evaluated in order: deny, then ask, then allow. MISSING: PROTECTED PATHS — the digest entirely missed that .claude/**, .mcp.json, .claude.json, .gitconfig, .pre-commit-config.yaml, .git, .husky, etc. are BUILT-IN protected paths: writes are never auto-approved in any mode except bypassPermissions, and permissions.allow CANNOT pre-approve them (the check runs before allow rules). This is the most important omission. | Auto mode drops broad allow rules on entry — on entering auto mode, Bash(*)/PowerShell(*)/wildcard-interpreter/package-run/Agent allow rules are DROPPED (restored on exit). A bundle that relies on a broad Bash allow for autonomous runs will behave differently under auto mode. A useful enterprise control the digest omitted (Kit only; N/A on Ultron Windows). | Read/Edit deny rules do NOT cover indirect file access — docs warn Read/Edit denies apply only to Claude's built-in file tools + recognized Bash file commands (cat/head/tail/sed), NOT arbitrary python/node scripts that open files. So 'Read(**/.env)' deny does NOT stop a Python script reading .env; OS sandbox is required for that (unavailable on Ultron's Windows). Material gap for the anticheat/secrets threat model. | WebFetch uses a separate context window and the built-in proxy does NOT do TLS inspection (domain-fronting bypass possible on broad allowlists like github.com). The digest treated Ultron as greenfield.

### Windows correctness of every proposed hook script in the enforcement bundle (jq presence, line endings, exit codes, path quoting, the single portable runtime). Adversarial lens applied to the board's hook-runtime claims for the Ultron Windows 11 host.
NET: Do NOT adopt the research's central prescription ("author all hooks in Node.js because it is always present"). On the Ultron native-Windows host that premise is REFUTED by official setup docs: the recommended Native/WinGet installs ship a self-contained binary and `claude` does not invoke Node — Node is required only for the optional `npm install -g` path. A node-based hook on a no-node host fails OPEN and silently, deleting every security gate (anticheat, secrets, SSRF, dangerous-git, ruff/mypy) while looking installed. That is the worst possible failure mode and it is a P0.

Replace "pick node" with "pick the verified runtime": (1) On Ultron, author hooks in shell form calling the project .venv/Scripts/python.exe (Python 3.11 is a hard dependency, reads stdin natively, behaves identically across OSes, no jq, no .cmd-shim trap), with Git Bash POSIX tools as a secondary path and CLAUDE_CODE_GIT_BASH_PATH set in settings.json. (2) For the cross-platform Kit, ship parallel bash+python and pwsh variants behind an OS guard. (3) Verify with `claude doctor` + a SessionStart self-test that asserts each hook's runtime exists and loudly warns via systemMessage if not.

Confirmed-correct Windows controls to KEEP: exit-2-vs-exit-0+JSON semantics; stop_hook_active (real, with a fixed 8-block cap — but the configurable CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP env var is unverified, treat as hallucinated); the `\"shell\":\"powershell\"` field; $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR; LF line endings via .gitattributes; the jq-absence warning (correct, but generalize it to a runtime-verification discipline, not "bash is unreliable").

Hard Windows hazards the research MISSED: the exec-form .cmd/.bat non-spawnable trap (breaks npx/eslint/ruff-shim hooks); PS 5.1 UTF-16/BOM stdout corrupting exit-0 JSON; and — most critically — the #46601 empty-stdin bug colliding with the no-node reality to make a Windows Stop hook unable to read its own keystone deadlock flag. For that case, fail OPEN (treat unreadable stdin as stop_hook_active=true / never block) and move real Stop-gate enforcement to CI, which is server-side and immune to both Windows hook breakage and disableAllHooks. Net: the bundle's teeth must live in CI; local Windows hooks are advisory + fast-deny only, authored in a runtime VERIFIED present on the box, never one assumed present.
- [refuted|P0] Node.js is ALWAYS available because Claude Code requires it / is the only guaranteed-available portable runtime; therefore author ALL hooks as Node.js .mjs invoked via `node ...`. (repeated across ~10 findings as the central runtime recommendation) => SAFER: Do NOT assume `node`. For the Ultron Windows host pick the runtime Claude Code itself guarantees: if Git for Windows is installed (the documented-recommended setup Ultron already relies on for the Bash tool), use shell-form bash hooks with POSIX tools Git Bash bundles (grep/sed present; jq NOT). If Git Bash is absent, Claude Code falls back to the PowerShell tool, so use `"shell":"powershell"`. The truly portable choice is a SHELL-FORM hook whose command is the project venv Python: `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.venv/Scripts/python.exe $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/hooks/gate.py` — Python 3.11 is a hard Ultron dependency, reads stdin via sys.stdin, OS-identical. Gate the choice on `claude doctor`, not the unverified node assumption. If node IS confirmed present, .mjs is fine as secondary. (Official setup docs refute the premise. The recommended Native installer, WinGet, and Linux package installs ship a self-contained native binary: 'The npm package installs the same native binary as the standalone installer ... The installed `claude` binary does not itself invoke )
- [overclaim|P1] On Windows the default shell is unreliable and bash 'may NOT be present' / bash+jq cannot be assumed; Node avoids the shell entirely. (framing throughout that bash is the exception on Windows) => SAFER: Treat the real risk as jq-absence, not bash-absence. Rewrite every jq-based hook to parse stdin JSON with the venv Python (json.load(sys.stdin)) or a tiny node one-liner ONLY if node is confirmed. Official docs: hook shell form runs via 'Git Bash on Windows, or PowerShell when Git Bash isn't installed,' and Git for Windows is RECOMMENDED ('so Claude Code can use the Bash tool'). So bash is the documented DEFAULT when present, not a rarity — )
- [conflict|P0] Stop hooks on Windows invoked via `pwsh -File` / `powershell.exe -File` receive EMPTY stdin (GH #46601), so stop_hook_active and all context are unavailable; the fix is to invoke Stop hooks via node instead. => SAFER: For the Stop gate on Windows: (1) verify the runtime with `claude doctor` and pick the one that actually reads stdin — if Git Bash is present, a bash Stop hook reads stdin fine and sidesteps #46601; (2) if you must use PowerShell, do NOT rely on stdin — read stop_hook_active defensively and treat unreadable input as stop_hook_active=true (exit 0 / never block), so a stdin-delivery bug fails OPEN not into deadlock; (3) keep real Stop-gate enforcement in CI (server-side, immune to the Windows stdin bug and disableAllHooks); local Stop hook stays advisory. Never let a Windows Stop hook block on a flag it cannot read. (The BUG is confirmed real (issue #46601, v2.1.101, Windows 11, both pwsh 7 and PS 5.1; [Console]::IsInputRedirected returns False; UserPromptSubmit with identical config works; closed not-planned/stale). But the prescribed FIX collides with the refuted node-availability claim: th)
- [overclaim|P1] Author hooks in exec form (`"command":"node"`, `"args":[...]`) to bypass shell-quoting; run tools like ruff/npx/eslint that way for cross-platform safety. => SAFER: In exec form on Windows point command at a real .exe: `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.venv/Scripts/python.exe` with args ["-m","ruff","check",...], or `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.venv/Scripts/ruff.exe` directly (ruff installs a real .exe in venv Scripts, not a .cmd shim). For tools that expose only a .cmd/.bat shim (npx, eslint), use shell form instead. Never exec-spawn npx/*.cmd by name on Windows. - [confirmed|P1] Hook scripts must have LF line endings; with git core.autocrlf=true, .sh hooks become CRLF and fail with 'bad interpreter'. - [confirmed|none] Exit code 2 hard-blocks; exit 1 / other non-zero codes are non-blocking (fail-open); exit 0 + JSON gives structured control; on exit 2 any stdout JSON is ignored. => SAFER: Keep the fail-open model but back hard gates with CI, because fail-open means any Windows runtime breakage silently disables the gate. For security-critical hooks, wrap the body so an internal error path still emits an explicit deny rather than crashing into a non-2 exit. (Verified verbatim: 'Claude Code only processes JSON on exit 0. If you exit 2, any JSON is ignored.' Exit 0 parses stdout JSON. - [confirmed|none] `"shell":"powershell"` is a valid hook field (bash|powershell), spawns PowerShell directly without CLAUDE_CODE_USE_POWERSHELL_TOOL, and is ignored when `args` is set. => SAFER: Where PowerShell is chosen, force pwsh 7 via exec form `"command":"pwsh","args":["-NoProfile","-File","$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/hooks/gate.ps1"]` to dodge PS 5.1 multibyte/module bugs — but remember #46601 (empty stdin) applies to pwsh, so do not use pwsh for the Stop gate's stdin parsing. - [confirmed|none] `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` resolves the project root in every hook subprocess (use it instead of hardcoded paths; on Windows it arrives with backslashes — use path.join). => SAFER: Reference hook scripts via `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/hooks/...` and build sub-paths with the runtime's path-join (os.path.join / Join-Path). In Git Bash forward slashes work; in PowerShell accept both. Avoid embedding raw C:\... literals. (Confirmed: '${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}: the project root' is set in the hook environment (and for stdio MCP servers / plugin LSP servers). Using it is correct portable-path practice; building sub-paths with the runtime's path-join rather than string concat is sound for Windows backsla)
- [confirmed|P2] Git Bash mangles Windows backslash paths (C:\Users\cl -> C:Userscl); PS 5.1 corrupts multibyte string literals / fails module loads vs pwsh 7; pwsh adds ~300-500ms startup vs ~10-50ms for bash/node. => SAFER: Never pass Windows backslash paths through a bash-form command string; use $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR with forward slashes. Use pwsh 7 (exec form, -NoProfile -File) not powershell.exe 5.1. Keep per-hook timeouts short and prefer one consolidated dispatcher to amortize startup on high-frequency PreToolUse hooks. (Real Windows-correctness hazards (sourced to a technically credible blog citing GH #5049/#16225/#22379, consistent with the official docs' own shell-tokenization warnings and PowerShell-tool preview limitations). They matter because they cause SILENT wrong-behavior, not loud erro)
- [refuted|P1] The portable hook bundle should ship a single universal runtime decided up front (Node.js for both Ultron and the cross-platform Kit). => SAFER: Prescribe a runtime DECISION PROCEDURE, not a single runtime: (1) Ultron -> shell-form hooks calling the project .venv Python (hard dep, stdin-native, OS-identical), Git Bash POSIX tools as fallback; (2) Kit -> ship parallel bash+python and pwsh variants behind an OS guard, document `claude doctor` as the verification step before trusting any gate. Mandate CI as the real backstop so the local-runtime choice is never the sole defense. (A single hardcoded runtime is the wrong model because Claude Code's own shell selection is conditional (Git Bash if present, else PowerShell tool) and node is not guaranteed. Picking ONE runtime blind guarantees breakage on some target hosts. The Kit is cross-platform; the Ultron)
MISSING: Runtime-presence VERIFICATION step: the research never tells you to confirm node/jq/git-bash on the target before trusting a hook. The bundle must run `claude doctor` and a one-time probe (which node; which jq; echo $CLAUDE_CODE_GIT_BASH_PATH) at setup and pick the runtime from the result, not from an assumption. | CLAUDE_CODE_GIT_BASH_PATH setting: official docs give an explicit settings.json env key to point Claude Code at Git Bash when auto-detection fails. Setting it makes bash-form hooks reliable on Ultron and was omitted entirely. | The exec-form .cmd/.bat trap on Windows (npx/eslint/ruff shims are not spawnable in exec form) — a concrete documented Windows breakage the research's exec-form advice ignores. | Fail-open-by-design is a SECURITY GAP on the wrong runtime: a missing-runtime hook exits non-2 / never spawns, so the gate silently disappears. The bundle needs a SessionStart self-test that asserts each enforcement hook's runtime is present and LOUDLY warns (systemMessage) if not — otherwise teeth silently vanish on Windows. | Python-venv-as-hook-runtime was never considered, despite Python 3.11 being a hard Ultron dependency and the most reliably-present, stdin-clean, OS-identical interpreter on that exact box (more reliable than node). | PowerShell tool preview limitations (profiles not loaded; sandboxing unsupported on Windows) and process-scope `-ExecutionPolicy Bypass` (respects MachinePolicy/UserPolicy Group Policy) — relevant if any PS hook assumes a profile-loaded env or assumes it can override enterprise execution policy. | UTF-8 BOM / encoding for stdout JSON: PS 5.1 emits UTF-16/BOM by default which can corrupt the JSON Claude Code parses on exit 0; any PowerShell hook returning structured JSON must force [Console]::OutputEncoding = UTF8 (no BOM). | No Windows contingency for the #46601 empty-stdin bug meaning a Windows Stop/SubagentStop hook may be unable to read stop_hook_active at all — the deadlock-prevention strategy has no fallback for its own keystone field being unreadable. | CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP env var (cited by the board as the configurable block cap) is NOT in the official Stop-input docs, which state a fixed '8 consecutive blocks' override — this configurable-cap claim is unverified/possibly hallucinated and should not be relied on (flagged because it touches the Stop-hook Windows reliability story).

### Security red-team of the gates — adversarial verification of the enforcement-bundle research (deny rules / SSRF / MCP / Stop-hook / managed-settings claims) against official Claude Code docs (code.claude.com), fetched and grepped 2026-06-20.
NET: The research is SUBSTANTIALLY CORRECT on my adversarial lens — most gate claims survive verification against official docs, and several of my early 'refutations' were artifacts of the WebFetch summary model returning false-negatives (it wrongly reported stop_hook_active, CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP, SUBPROCESS_ENV_SCRUB, USE_POWERSHELL_TOOL and EXPERIMENTAL_AGENT_TEAMS as 'NOT PRESENT' when raw-markdown grep confirmed all of them exist). Lesson for the synthesis step: trust grep over summaries for presence/absence. CONFIRMED and safe to build on: deny-first precedence and bare-vs-scoped deny semantics; disableBypassPermissionsMode/disableAutoMode work in ANY scope (so project-scope IS effective for solo Ultron — the mission anchor's 'managed-only' framing is imprecise); WebFetch domain-wildcard rules and their NON-inspection of resolved IP; stop_hook_active + the 8-block cap (configurable via CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP); native-Windows has NO sandbox; the MCP auto-enable CVEs are real (both CVE-2025-59536 and CVE-2026-21852); deny mcp__* then literal-server allow; Node exec-form hooks; if-field fails open. FIX BEFORE SHIPPING — five P1s: (1) the SSRF IP blocklist is INCOMPLETE — add 0/8, 100.64/10, 198.18/15, ::1, ::ffff:0:0/96 (unwrap IPv4-mapped), fe80::/10, the GCP/Azure metadata hostnames, and accept the hook cannot IP-pin built-in WebFetch (no true rebinding closure on Windows). (2) PostToolUse decision:block ENDS THE TURN unless continueOnBlock:true — every proposed PostToolUse quality gate must use additionalContext (advisory) or set continueOnBlock, or it silently kills autonomous turns (violates the zero-autonomy-loss mandate). (3) Do NOT ship a WorktreeCreate hook in the Kit — it REPLACES git worktree creation and will break worktrees for every consumer; leave default git behavior intact. (4) Never bare-deny WebFetch/WebSearch in the Kit (kills deep research, a must-not-block capability); and 'curl'/'wget' are Bash invocations, not tools — they can only be scoped-denied, with the interpreter-wrap class (python -c/node -e/bash -c, env-runners like devbox run/npx) remaining genuinely uncatchable by string matching on native Windows. (5) The Read(.env)/Read(~/.ssh) deny does NOT stop script-level file reads and there is no OS settings-file protection on native Windows — Ultron's real airtight gates are CI + the Python import-firewall, not permission rules. ARCHITECTURE: layer exactly as the research says — deny-first permission rules (coarse, fast, un-overridable from project scope) + Node PreToolUse hooks (best-effort interpreter/SSRF scan, fail-closed) + advisory PostToolUse additionalContext (capped at ~300 chars / hard 10k cap) + Stop hook with stop_hook_active+background_tasks/session_crons guards scoped to current-turn git diff + CI required status checks as the ONLY un-overridable gate (because disableAllHooks, bypassPermissions, and the 8-block override all defeat in-session hooks). This achieves maximum teeth with no loss of autonomous capability, worktrees, MCP, deep research, or user-directed canon maintenance (gate canon/settings/hook edits with ASK, never DENY).
- [confirmed|none] disableBypassPermissionsMode and disableAutoMode work from ANY settings scope (user/project/local/managed); they are most authoritative in managed but not managed-only. => SAFER: Set permissions.disableBypassPermissionsMode:"disable" and permissions.disableAutoMode:"disable" in BOTH project .claude/settings.json (effective for the solo Ultron box) AND, where an org wants it un-overridable, in managed-settings.json / HKLM. Do not claim project-scope is a no-op. (Official permissions page states verbatim: 'disableBypassPermissionsMode is typically placed in managed settings to enforce organizational policy, but it works from any scope. A user can set it in their own settings to lock themselves out of bypass mode.' Value is the string "dis)
- [confirmed|none] A bare deny rule (e.g. "Bash", "WebSearch") removes the tool from Claude's context entirely; a scoped deny ("Bash(rm *)") leaves the tool available and blocks only matches. Bash(*) == bare Bash. => SAFER: For Ultron's anticheat web-silence: deny Bash(curl *), Bash(wget *), PowerShell(Invoke-WebRequest *), PowerShell(Invoke-RestMethod *) AS SCOPED rules, and gate WebFetch via a domain allowlist + PreToolUse SSRF hook rather than a bare WebFetch deny — preserves the tool for the rare allowed fetch. For the Kit, NEVER bare-deny WebFetch/WebSearch. (Official text: 'A bare tool name like Bash removes the tool from Claude's context entirely, so Claude never sees it. A scoped rule like Bash(rm *) leaves the tool available... Bash(*) is equivalent to Bash and matches all Bash commands. As a deny rule, both forms remove the tool )
- [confirmed|P1] Bash curl/wget bypass WebFetch domain rules; Bash arg-constraining patterns (Bash(curl http://github.com/ *)) are fragile and bypassable via option-ordering, protocol swap, redirects, $VAR indirection, extra spaces. => SAFER: Defense in depth: (1) scoped deny curl/wget/Invoke-WebRequest; (2) PreToolUse Node hook that scans the FULL command for interpreter-wrap patterns (\b(bash|sh|pwsh|python|node)\b.*-(c|e)\b.*(curl|wget|urllib|requests|http)) and denies; (3) accept that string-scanning cannot catch runtime interpreter exfil — rely on OS sandbox egress allowlist on macOS/Linux, and on Windows accept the hook is best-effort and back it with the Python import-firewall + CI secrets scan. (Official Warning box enumerates exactly these bypasses verbatim ('Options before URL', 'Different protocol', 'Redirects', 'Variables: URL=http://github.com && curl $URL', 'Extra spaces') and states 'using WebFetch alone does not prevent network access. If Bash is allowed, Claude )
- [confirmed|none] WebFetch(domain:*.example.com) matches any-depth subdomain but NOT the apex; example.* crosses only ONE dot segment (blocks subdomain-registration attacks); matching is hostname-only and does NOT inspect resolved IP. => SAFER: Keep WebFetch(domain:...) as the first-pass allowlist AND add the PreToolUse DNS-resolution IP-classification hook for the second layer, exactly as the research recommends — but fix the IP-range completeness gap (see next verdict). (Official WebFetch section confirms each clause verbatim, including 'In any position other than a leading *. or a bare *, the wildcard matches only the text between two dots... This keeps a trailing wildcard from matching domains an attacker could register.' Crucially it confirms )
- [overclaim|P1] The SSRF-guard PreToolUse hook must reject RFC-1918 / loopback / link-local / cloud-metadata ranges, resolving DNS at connection time (decimal/IPv6/DNS-rebinding bypass string-match). => SAFER: Block ALL of: 0.0.0.0/8, 10/8, 100.64/10, 127/8, 169.254/16, 172.16/12, 192.0.0/24, 192.168/16, 198.18/15, ::1/128, ::/128, fc00::/7, fe80::/10, ::ffff:0:0/96 (unwrap IPv4-mapped before classifying), and the literal hosts metadata.google.internal / 169.254.169.254 / fd00:ec2::254. Resolve with {all:true} and reject if ANY address is private. Treat the hook as best-effort (cannot IP-pin built-in WebFetch) and pair with sandbox.network.allowedDomains on macOS/Linux. Fail CLOSED on DNS error/timeout. (The DIRECTION is correct and well-sourced, but the research's enumerated CIDR list is INCOMPLETE and would leave SSRF holes — failing my lens question 'are the cloud-metadata/RFC-1918 checks complete (IPv6, link-local, alternate encodings)?'. The list omits: IPv6 Unique-Local fc0)
- [conflict|P1] sandbox.network.allowedDomains does NOT restrict WebFetch (only Bash subprocesses); a WebFetch permission allow rule can bypass sandbox network restriction (GH#31296), making the sandbox LESS restrictive than expected for WebFetch on the lethal-trifecta egress leg. => SAFER: On macOS/Linux Kit deployments use allowManagedDomainsOnly + an explicit allowedDomains list (which now governs both Bash and WebFetch per the managed table) as defense-in-depth, plus the SSRF hook. Verify against the live #31296 status before relying on either direction. On native Windows (Ultron) the sandbox is unavailable regardless. (PARTIALLY refuted by current docs. - [confirmed|none] Stop/SubagentStop self-deadlock is prevented by checking stop_hook_active (boolean in stdin JSON, true when Claude is already in forced continuation); a Stop hook must exit 0 / not block when it is true. => SAFER: Every Stop/SubagentStop hook: first line reads stdin JSON and `if (input.stop_hook_active) process.exit(0)`; also early-exit 0 if background_tasks.length || session_crons.length is non-empty. - [confirmed|none] PostToolUse additionalContext is nested under hookSpecificOutput, and the canon ENFORCEMENT.md example that puts additionalContext at top-level is WRONG. => SAFER: For advisory legacy-file lint, use exit 0 + hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext (never block). - [confirmed|none] PreToolUse 'defer' returns a decision value that pauses/exits the session for headless --resume; using it in interactive (Ultron) would terminate the session, so never use defer interactively. => SAFER: Use deny for hard gates, ask for sensitive-but-legitimate (canon edits), allow for pre-approved. - [confirmed|none] enableAllProjectMcpServers:true / enabledMcpjsonServers in committed project settings were the root cause of CVE-2025-59536 (auto-activating a malicious repo .mcp.json → RCE / API-token exfil); never set them in a committed file; deny mcp__* then selectively allow. => SAFER: Never set enableAllProjectMcpServers:true or populate enabledMcpjsonServers in committed .claude/settings.json. - [version-uncertain|P1] disableAllHooks:true in .claude/settings.local.json bypasses even managed-tier hooks (GH#26637, HIGH, closed-without-fix), so within-session hooks cannot be the sole gate — CI required. => SAFER: Make CI required status checks (with 'do not allow bypassing') the authoritative gate for no-test-deletion, secrets, lockfile, ruff/mypy-on-changed. Use within-session hooks for fast feedback only. (disableAllHooks EXISTS as a real setting (settings page: 'Disable all hooks and any custom status line').
