- [confirmed|none] The 'if' field does shell-aware subcommand parsing but FAILS OPEN when the command can't be parsed — so it must be a perf filter, never the security gate. => SAFER: Use if only to reduce spawns (broad like Bash(git *)); put the actual deny logic inside the Node hook body AND in permissions.deny. Never rely on if-narrowing as a control. (Official: 'The filter also fails open, running your hook regardless of pattern, when the Bash command cannot be parsed. Because the if filter is best-effort, use the permission system rather than a hook to enforce a hard allow or deny.' Fully validates the research. The real enfo)
- [confirmed|none] Author all Windows hooks as Node.js exec-form ("command":"node","args":[...]); bash+jq is unreliable on Windows; pwsh Stop hooks may receive empty stdin (GH#46601). => SAFER: All shared hooks: Node .mjs via exec form, read stdin with fs.readFileSync(0,'utf8') in try/catch defaulting to {}. Reserve shell:"powershell"/pwsh exec-form only for genuinely PS-native side effects (toast, VoiceMeeter COM). Add .gitattributes *.mjs/*.sh text eol=lf. (Docs confirm exec form bypasses the shell and is 'Required on Windows for .cmd/.bat shim files (use node + script path instead)'; default shell on Windows is Git Bash or PowerShell; jq is not guaranteed (the hooks-guide jq examples carry an install note). Node is guaranteed becau)
MISSING: Hook output SIZE CAP (10,000 chars) and large-output spill-to-file: confirmed in hooks.md line 704 ('Hook output strings, including additionalContext, systemMessage, and plain stdout, are capped at 10,000 characters. Output that exceeds this limit is saved to a file and replaced with a preview'). The research's PostToolUse ruff/mypy advisory hooks MUST cap additionalContext (~300 chars) or they spill — the research mentions this only in passing for one finding; it is a global constraint on every context-injecting hook. | continueOnBlock:true for PostToolUse — entirely absent from the research. Without it, a PostToolUse decision:block ENDS THE TURN (warning line), it does not 'softly nudge'. Any quality-gate hook the research proposes on PostToolUse will silently kill autonomous turns. This is a P1 omission for the 'zero loss of autonomy' requirement. | CLAUDE_CODE_POWERSHELL_RESPECT_EXECUTION_POLICY — the real Windows knob: by default Claude Code passes -ExecutionPolicy Bypass when spawning PowerShell for hooks/statusline. On locked-down corporate Windows this matters for whether .ps1 hooks run at all; the research never mentions it. | CLAUDE_CODE_SHELL_PREFIX — a session-wide command-wrapper env var that wraps EVERY Bash/hook/MCP-startup command. This is both an audit-logging opportunity (the research wants a local JSONL tool-call audit for Ultron) AND an injection surface (a malicious value runs before every command). Omitted entirely. | CLAUDE_CODE_SCRIPT_CAPS — per-session script invocation caps that work alongside SUBPROCESS_ENV_SCRUB (e.g. {"deploy.sh":2}). A real, supported supply-chain/anti-runaway control the research missed; relevant to capping autonomous mammoth runs. | Symlink permission semantics: deny rules block if EITHER the symlink path OR its resolved target matches, while allow rules require BOTH to match (and otherwise fall back to prompting). This is an SSRF/exfil-relevant detail (a symlink in an allowed dir pointing at ~/.ssh is denied) the research omitted — it strengthens the Read(.env)/Read(~/.ssh) deny posture. | WebSearch allowed_domains/blocked_domains are TOOL PARAMETERS, and Tool(param:value) deny/ask matching is documented — but the doc explicitly says command/file_path/url/path/notebook_path fields are NOT param-matchable (Bash(command:rm *) is ignored with a startup warning). The research's idea of param-level gating needs this caveat: you cannot deny WebFetch by url-param, only by WebFetch(domain:). | Process-wrapper stripping for Bash deny matching: Claude Code strips timeout/time/nice/nohup/stdbuf and bare xargs before matching, but does NOT strip env-runners (devbox run, mise exec, npx, docker exec) — so Bash(devbox run *) grants whatever follows 'run' including rm -rf. Any anticheat/dangerous-command deny set must enumerate these runner-escape vectors; the research's deny lists ignore them. | Read/Edit deny rules do NOT cover arbitrary subprocesses (a python/node script that opens .env itself bypasses Read(.env)). The docs state this explicitly and point to the sandbox for OS-level path enforcement. On native Windows (no sandbox) this is an unclosable gap for Ultron — the research treats Read(.env) deny as airtight; it is not against script-level reads. | The Elicitation / ElicitationResult hook events (MCP server requests user input) CAN block and are a real injection surface (a malicious MCP server can drive an elicitation). The research's 30-event catalog lists them but proposes no control; an Elicitation gate is a frontier control worth adding. | Settings-file self-protection under sandbox: the sandbox auto-denies writes to settings.json at every scope and the managed dir — but this is sandbox-only, i.e. NOT on native Windows Ultron. The research's ConfigChange-hook tamper-detection is the right Windows substitute but should be paired with the documented fact that there is NO OS-level settings protection on Windows. | PreToolUse permissionDecision:'allow' does NOT suppress deny/ask rules (deny-first always wins) — confirmed in docs. The research correctly says hooks can't override deny, but should also flag that a hook 'allow' cannot be used to carve an exception out of a broad deny rule (the deny-cannot-carry-allow-exception rule applies to hooks too), which closes a tempting but broken design. | No mention of WebFetch's built-in separate-context-window safeguard for fetched content (documented on /security) as a baseline anti-injection mitigation that already exists — relevant to not over-engineering the WebFetch SSRF/injection hook.

### Maintenance & adherence-cliff lens on the Frontier Claude Code enforcement bundle (settings.json + .claude/hooks/** + ruff/mypy + tests/test_map.txt + CI), for Ultron/Kenning (Windows 11, Python 3.11, runs beside Vanguard) and the portable kit. Verdicts cite official code.claude.com/docs pages fetched this session.
NET: SHRINK, DON'T STACK. Through the maintenance/adherence-cliff lens the proposed bundle is over-built and will degrade adherence and cause churn. (1) Keep the ALWAYS-ON surface tiny: 5-8 hard invariants in the lean root CLAUDE.md only; demote the full BR/P/T canon + CONSTRAINTS to path-scoped .claude/rules/ and on-demand skills; do NOT re-inject the canon via SessionStart+UserPromptSubmit+PostCompact+claudeMd simultaneously (pick one). Add a mechanical line/token-budget gate so it cannot re-bloat. (2) Collapse ~15 hooks into TWO Node.js dispatchers (PreToolUse: anticheat+secrets+dangerous-git; PostToolUse: ruff/mypy ADVISORY via nested hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext + stub-scan-on-diff) plus ONE Stop gate (Node .mjs, stop_hook_active guard FIRST, scoped to changed files, CI-backed). Every hook fail-OPEN (exit 0 on error) so a live game is never silenced. (3) FIX the two confirmed canon defects now: ruff format(write)->--check, and additionalContext nesting; grandfather orchestrator.py via extend-per-file-ignores + mypy ignore_errors. (4) Correct two factual errors before shipping: there is NO 'delegate' defaultMode (use 'default'); disableAllHooks does NOT bypass managed hooks from local scope (docs say the opposite) -- re-justify CI as the backstop on correct grounds (server-side immunity + solo Ultron has no managed tier). (5) Keep heavyweight prompt-injection machinery (SSRF/taint/spotlighting/MELON) OUT of Ultron (no web in hot path) and OPT-IN/OFF-by-default for the kit. (6) Network bare-denies are Ultron-gaming-profile ONLY (settings.local.json), never shared, to preserve deep-research/WebFetch for the kit and non-gaming sessions; never bare-deny Agent or mcp__*. (7) Managed-only keys belong in a SEPARATE managed-settings.json template, not committed project settings, to avoid false-security dead config on the solo box. Net: maximum teeth comes from a FEW correct, fail-open, Node-authored, CI-backed gates -- not a large always-loaded canon and a dozen speculative hooks.
- [confirmed|P1] The always-loaded root CLAUDE.md must be kept lean (~150-line adherence cliff); the bundle's SessionStart/UserPromptSubmit context injection + verbose canon (BR-0..BR-21, P1-P22, T.1-T.14, CONSTRAINTS) risks bloating context past reliable instruction-following. => SAFER: Pick ONE always-on channel. Put 5-8 hard invariants (anticheat firewall, run_tests.py wrapper, no-secrets, canon-wins) in the lean root CLAUDE.md only; demote full BR/P/T canon + CONSTRAINTS to path-scoped .claude/rules/ and on-demand skills that load lazily, NOT into SessionStart/UserPromptSubmit which fire every session/turn. Add a mechanical line/token-budget gate. (Instruction-overload is the biggest maintenance hazard here. The digest proposes FOUR always-on grounding channels (root CLAUDE.md + SessionStart additionalContext + UserPromptSubmit per-turn reminder + PostCompact re-inject + managed claudeMd), all consuming the same context bud)
- [overclaim|P1] Every hook in the bundle is justified by a real observed failure (two-strikes); the ~15-hook set (anticheat, secrets, ruff-fix, ruff/mypy, stub-scan, SSRF guard, taint tracker, spotlighting, ConfigChange audit, SubagentStop logger, WorktreeCreate, PreCompact, PostCompact, statusLine, asyncRewake test-runner) is not cargo-cult. => SAFER: Ship ONE Node.js PreToolUse dispatcher (anticheat+secrets+dangerous-git) and ONE PostToolUse dispatcher (ruff/mypy advisory + stub-scan-on-diff) = 2 spawns/call max, per the digest's own one-dispatcher guidance. Defer SSRF/taint/spotlighting to the KIT only, env-flag-gated OFF by default; drop them from Ultron until an incident occurs. (~15 hooks exceeds the digest's own 3-5 production ceiling. Half defend threats with zero observed incidents in a fully-local, voice-first, web-denied-while-gaming assistant (SSRF DNS-rebinding, CaMeL taint, spotlighting, MELON are browser-agent defenses imported into an offline g)
- [confirmed|P0] Stop hooks must check stop_hook_active in stdin JSON to avoid self-deadlock; the harness enforces an 8-block cap overridable via CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP. => SAFER: First line of every Stop/SubagentStop hook: read stdin, if stop_hook_active is true exit 0. Scope to current-turn changed files via git diff. Back with the CI gate (cannot deadlock) so the Stop hook can safely no-op. Do not hardcode 8. Cite the hooks-GUIDE URL in comments, not the reference. (VERIFIED on the official hooks-GUIDE page ('Stop hook hits the block cap'): 'Claude Code overrides a Stop hook after it blocks 8 times in a row without progress... Parse the stop_hook_active field... exit early if true', and 'raise the cap with CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP'. T)
- [confirmed|P1] The canon ENFORCEMENT.md post-edit hook runs 'ruff format <file>' (WRITE mode), which on the 10,700-line orchestrator.py reformats unmodified lines on every edit, breaking surgical diffs and git blame. => SAFER: Use 'ruff format --check' and 'ruff check --no-fix' (advisory via additionalContext, never auto-mutate tracked files). Grandfather orchestrator.py via extend-per-file-ignores (ruff) and [[tool.mypy.overrides]] ignore_errors=true. Only auto-fix files not yet tracked by git. Never run ruff format(write) or project-wide mypy from a per-edit hook. (Worst maintenance defect in the existing canon and directly on my lens. Auto-formatting a legacy monolith per-edit creates noise diffs, defeats the surgical-edit requirement the mission calls non-negotiable, can silently introduce unrequested regressions, and risks an infinite ch)

Pair with a PreToolUse additionalContext note explaining WHY the file is sensitive so the gate educates rather than nags. Ultron runs live beside a kernel anti-cheat; a fail-CLOSED hook could silence Ultron mid-game. The bundle needs a documented one-line disable (managed-level disableAllHooks, or removing the hooks block) and every hook must be provably fail-OPEN (exit 0 on any parse error / missing dep). This operational-safety control is mentioned only in passing, not made a first-class deliverable. | TEST_MAP STALENESS OWNERSHIP. tests/test_map.txt for the dynamic-dispatch orchestrator.py will silently rot. ### Compaction-survival hook set (PreCompact snapshot + PostCompact + SessionStart reground) for the Frontier Kit / Ultron enforcement bundle
NET: The compaction-survival hook set must be RESTRUCTURED: the research's core prescription — re-inject CONSTRAINTS/anticheat via PostCompact additionalContext — is REFUTED by official docs (PostCompact has no decision control and cannot inject context; it is side-effects only). Wiring it produces a silent no-op, which is the most dangerous failure mode because it looks correct. Correct, verified set: (1) PreCompact (matchers manual+auto, NEVER decision:block) writes a best-effort snapshot of STATUS.md + a tight CONSTRAINTS/BR-0..BR-21 + anticheat-stance digest to .claude/snapshots/last_precompact.md and exits 0 always. (2) SessionStart (this is the ONLY context-injection vehicle that survives compaction) with source=='compact' reads that snapshot and emits it as additionalContext/stdout; on missing snapshot it falls back to reading docs/canon/BINDING_RULES.md directly. Gate the heavy dump to source in {compact, resume} and always inject a 1-line anticheat reminder on startup; cap the payload (<~500 words) to avoid a compaction feedback loop. (3) PostCompact, if used at all, only LOGS that compaction occurred and deletes stale snapshots — no context, no block. All three authored as Node.js .mjs (readFileSync(0) + try/catch → exit 0) to dodge the Windows pwsh empty-stdin bug. This set is inherently self-deadlock-free (SessionStart/PostCompact can't block; PreCompact never blocks). No conflict with existing flow: it is additive and fail-open, and it does NOT touch permission rules, so it cannot false-block user-directed canon/settings edits. Treat 'only root CLAUDE.md survives compaction' as unverified-but-plausible (issue #59309 confirms rule weakening); the reground is justified regardless. Ship a documented manual /compact smoke test as the only feasible backstop, since the dominant risk is silent no-op rather than over-blocking.
- [refuted|P1] Wire a PostCompact hook (advisory-only) that emits additionalContext re-injecting the CONSTRAINTS.md summary so Claude is re-grounded immediately after compaction. => SAFER: Do all post-compaction reground via the SessionStart hook with matcher 'compact' (source=='compact'), NOT PostCompact. SessionStart's stdout is added to context and it supports hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext. Reserve PostCompact strictly for side effects (logging that a compaction happened, cleaning snapshot temp files). If you want belt-and-suspenders, have PreCompact write the CONSTRAINTS/STATUS snapshot to a temp file and have the SessionStart(compact) hook read that file and emit it as additionalContext. (Official hooks docs list PostCompact under 'No decision control' / side-effects only: on exit 2 it 'Shows stderr to user only' and it is NOT in the set of events that support hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext injection. A PostCompact hook returning additionalContext is silentl)
- [confirmed|none] SessionStart fires on session startup, resume, /clear, and post-compact (matcher 'compact'); its additionalContext is injected as a system reminder before the first model request, making it the correct reground vehicle after compaction. => SAFER: Keep SessionStart(matcher:'compact') as the primary reground. For ergonomics, gate the heavy CONSTRAINTS dump to source=='compact' || source=='resume' (not every 'startup') to avoid burning context on fresh sessions where root CLAUDE.md already loaded. Cap additionalContext to a tight BR-0..BR-21 + anticheat-stance summary (<~500 words) so it does not itself accelerate the next compaction. (Confirmed verbatim against the official lifecycle/matcher tables: SessionStart matchers are startup/resume/clear/compact; 'compact' = 'Auto or manual compaction'. Input carries source=='compact'. Author it in Node.js (.mjs) read via readFileSync(0,'utf8') for Windows/Ultron — pwsh -File Stop/Session hooks have the empty-stdin bug (issue #46601), so Node is the safe runtime. (Official decision-control table: SessionStart 'Can block? No', exit 2 'Shows stderr to user only'. Have SessionStart(compact) consume the snapshot; if the snapshot is missing (PreCompact didn't fire), fall back to reading docs/canon/BINDING_RULES.md directly. (PreCompact exists with matchers manual/auto. It CAN block (top-level decision), but the digest's prescribed usage explicitly omits decision:block and only does file snapshots, so there is no blocking/self-deadlock risk. The snapshot is the right way to preserve state that the Ses)
- [overclaim|P1] PreCompact 'with only file-snapshot side-effects (no decision:block) is zero-blocking-risk' — implying a blocking PreCompact would be a reasonable hard gate. => SAFER: Never return decision:block from PreCompact on the 'auto' matcher. If you ever block, scope strictly to matcher:'manual' (user typed /compact) AND make the condition trivially satisfiable in one step, AND back it with a max-attempt guard. ### Completeness critic (adversarial lens): what frontier/enterprise enforcement controls did the research OMIT, and are the few controls it DID claim about audit/redaction/injection actually real?
NET: The research's enforcement architecture is fundamentally sound and largely verified against official docs — the 30-event catalog, the deny>ask>allow precedence, stop_hook_active, OTEL audit, claudeMd/allowManagedHooksOnly, and the Node.js-over-jq Windows rule all check out. But as a completeness critic I find THREE material gaps and ONE refutation that must change the bundle. REFUTATION (P1): 'PostToolUse additionalContext is broken (#3983)' is false per the current Hooks reference — it is the documented, supported, zero-friction advisory channel and should be the bundle's DEFAULT for lint/type/stub/redaction nudges; do not route those to exit-2+stderr. GAPS (highest value first): (1) Ultron needs a LOCAL Node JSONL audit hook (PostToolUse, async) + updatedToolOutput secret redaction — the research gave OTEL (Kit-only) but no anticheat-safe local equivalent. (2) The bundle has no self-integrity: hooks/settings reload mid-session with no native signing or snapshot, so a prompt-injected settings.json rewrite silently disarms the gate — add a SessionStart hash-manifest + ConfigChange ADVISORY diff (never block, to preserve user-directed canon maintenance) + a CI check that fails if deny entries shrink. (3) The CI backstop is not optional decoration — it is the only layer disableAllHooks (#26637) and bypassPermissions cannot defeat; ship it as required, SHA-pinned, changed-files-scoped status checks. Two anti-footguns to bake into the design rules: every hook must be jq-free Node, idempotent, short-timeout, and fail-OPEN (exit 0 on parse error) so a hook crash never silences Ultron mid-game; and all file-protection on canon/settings/hooks must be ASK (or advisory ConfigChange), never DENY, so the user can always direct Claude to edit them. Net: adopt the research, but flip the additionalContext verdict, add the local-audit + redaction + self-integrity + CI-required trio, and treat OTEL/managed-only keys as Kit-enterprise-only with Ultron falling back to project deny rules + Node hooks + CI.
- [refuted|P1] PostToolUse JSON output via hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext is 'confirmed broken in Claude Code' (issue #3983, closed-not-planned); the workaround is to write to stderr + exit 2, or use the Stop hook instead. => SAFER: Use PostToolUse additionalContext as the DEFAULT advisory channel for ruff/mypy/stub nudges. Keep exit-2 only for the PreToolUse hard gates. If you ever observe the MCP-tool edge case, fall back to a Stop-hook additionalContext summary — not to stderr-as-API. (The official Hooks reference explicitly documents additionalContext working for PostToolUse: 'Claude Code wraps the string in a system reminder and inserts it into the conversation at the point where the hook fired... PreToolUse, PostToolUse, PostToolUseFailure, and PostToolBatch)
- [version-uncertain|P1] Hook integrity/signing exists or can be relied on natively; a 'signed hooks' / hash-allowlist control is part of the available toolkit. => SAFER: Build the integrity layer yourself: a SessionStart hook that hashes .claude/settings.json + every .claude/hooks/* into a committed manifest, plus a ConfigChange hook (matcher project_settings/local_settings) that diffs the permissions.deny array and the hooks block and injects additionalContext (advisory, never block — user-directed canon edits must not be false-blocked) when a deny rule or hook is removed. Back it with the CI guard that fails if settings.json deny entries shrink. (Hook signing / cryptographic integrity / hash-allowlist is NOT documented anywhere in settings or hooks reference. Flag so no one wires secret-scrubbing to MessageDisplay and gets a false sense of safety. | PLUGIN/MARKETPLACE TRUST: strictKnownMarketplaces + strictPluginOnlyCustomization (managed-only) and the CVE-2026-21852 enableAllProjectMcpServers auto-activation hole. Research touched MCP but did not assemble the plugin-supply-chain block (block enableAllProjectMcpServers:true in committed settings; deny mcp__* then selectively allow). | CI BACKSTOP is the ONLY override-proof layer: disableAllHooks in settings.local.json can defeat even managed hooks (#26637), and bypassPermissions skips non-managed PreToolUse. Therefore the no-test-deletion / ruff-changed / mypy-changed / secrets-diff / lockfile guards MUST exist as required GitHub status checks with 'do not allow bypassing', and every third-party action pinned to a full commit SHA (CVE-2025-30066). This is a structural requirement, not optional. | CLAUDE_CODE_SUBPROCESS_ENV_SCRUB=1 in the launch env to strip ANTHROPIC_API_KEY / cloud creds from Bash subprocesses — defense-in-depth against the lethal-trifecta exfil leg; entirely omitted. | DSP/anticheat-adjacent runtime concern: hook overhead budget on the live game path. Pin explicit short timeouts (PreToolUse 5s, UserPromptSubmit <=5s) and consolidate to a single Node dispatcher (<=2 process spawns/tool call) so the enforcement bundle never adds latency during a live Valorant round.

### Claude Code enforcement bundle (.claude/settings.json + hooks + ruff/mypy + test_map + CI) for (1) Ultron/Kenning Windows 11 voice assistant and (2) the portable Frontier Claude Code Kit. Adversarial zero-loss go/no-go review of the 20-facet research digest.
NET: The research is ~80% sound and the high-stakes anchors (deny>ask>allow precedence, stop_hook_active + 8-block cap + CLAUDE_CODE_STOP_HOOK_BLOCK_CAP, defaultMode auto ignored in project scope since v2.1.142, bypass protected-paths since v2.1.126, classifier 3/20 abort, WorktreeCreate replaces git, jq-absent-on-Windows, managed-only keys, sandbox-not-on-native-Windows) are CONFIRMED against official docs. Build the bundle on these. THREE corrections are mandatory before shipping: (1) P1 REFUTE the GH#26637 'disableAllHooks bypasses MANAGED hooks' claim — current docs say managed hooks survive local disableAllHooks; keep CI as the unoverrideable backstop for the correct reason (non-managed hooks are locally disable-able / --dangerously-skip-permissions defeats them), and put truly-critical hooks in managed settings with allowManagedHooksOnly. (2) P1 NO-GO on any DENY of WebFetch/WebSearch or .claude/canon edits: both directly violate the zero-loss requirement (Kit needs deep research; the user routinely runs research AND edits canon FROM the Ultron repo) — and .claude is already a protected path so a deny is both redundant and harmful. Use scoped Bash(curl/wget) denies + a fail-closed Node SSRF PreToolUse guard instead, and gate network only via a live-game settings.local.json profile. (3) P1 the existing canon ENFORCEMENT.md `ruff format` WRITE-mode hook MUST become `ruff format --check` + `ruff check --no-fix` advisory-only on the single tool_input.file_path, with orchestrator.py grandfathered via extend-per-file-ignores and mypy ignore_errors=true — otherwise every edit reformats the legacy monolith (churn). Additional must-dos: design around PROTECTED PATHS (do not duplicate/deny them); run run_tests.py via asyncRewake not synchronously; author ALL hooks as Node .mjs exec-form with pinned short timeouts behind matcher+if; treat the auto-mode false-positive %, the TDAD 70% figure, the specific CVE ids, and the version-pinned GH regressions (#39344/#52822/#46601/#31296) as UNVERIFIED — keep their sound operational conclusions but strip the unconfirmed numbers/ids from the shipped docs. Net: maximum teeth via (managed) deny rules for pip/curl/secrets + Node PreToolUse guards + advisory PostToolUse lint + a deadlock-guarded current-turn-scoped Stop hook + an unoverrideable SHA-pinned CI gate, with ZERO bare-tool denies, ZERO denies on user-directed canon/network work, and ZERO synchronous long-running hooks. This achieves the hard requirement; the only genuine NO-GOs in the digest are the WebFetch/canon denies and the write-mode formatter."}
- [confirmed|none] 30 hook events exist; the named blocking set includes PostToolBatch, PermissionRequest, UserPromptExpansion, ConfigChange, TeammateIdle, TaskCreated/Completed, Elicitation/ElicitationResult, WorktreeCreate; and the advisory set includes SessionStart, PostCompact, InstructionsLoaded, WorktreeRemove, etc. => SAFER: Cite the catalog by name, not by a fixed count; pin the few events you actually wire (SessionStart, PreToolUse, PostToolUse, Stop, SubagentStop, ConfigChange, PreCompact/PostCompact) which are all stable. (The official hooks reference lists this catalog with the same event names and blocking/advisory split (PreToolUse, UserPromptSubmit, UserPromptExpansion, PermissionRequest, Stop, SubagentStop, PostToolUse, PostToolUseFailure, PostToolBatch, ConfigChange, PreCompact, TeammateIdle,)
- [confirmed|none] Permission precedence is deny > ask > allow, first-match wins, rules MERGE (union) across all five settings layers, a deny rule CANNOT carry allow-exceptions, and deny from ANY scope blocks regardless of allow elsewhere. => SAFER: Place hard denies (.env, secrets, pip/curl/wget) in project .claude/settings.json so they merge with user rules; never attempt a narrower allow carve-out. (Verbatim: 'Rules are evaluated in order: deny, then ask, then allow... a deny rule cannot carry allowlist exceptions.' and 'If a tool is denied at any level, no other level can allow it.' Settings precedence (managed > CLI > local > project > user) and the deny-from-any-scope rul)

(Verbatim: 'set permissions.disableBypassPermissionsMode or permissions.disableAutoMode to "disable" in any settings file. These are most useful in managed settings where they cannot be overridden.' and 'disableBypassPermissionsMode ... works from any scope. A user can set it in t)

- [confirmed|none] PostToolUse is advisory-only and cannot block; it supports updatedToolOutput and additionalContext; to halt the loop use PostToolBatch (decision:block). => SAFER: Use PostToolUse additionalContext for ruff/mypy nudges (zero friction); use PostToolUse decision:block sparingly as a soft veto; use PostToolBatch decision:block for true loop halts. (The reference confirms PostToolUse runs after execution (cannot undo the edit) and supports updatedToolOutput/additionalContext, and that PostToolBatch fires once before the next model call and supports decision:block. - [confirmed|P1] The canon ENFORCEMENT.md PostToolUse hook runs `ruff format "$f"` in WRITE mode, which reformats whole legacy files (orchestrator.py ~10,700 lines) on every edit — violating surgical-diff and creating churn. Use `ruff format --check` and `ruff check --no-fix` advisory-only instead. => SAFER: PostToolUse: `ruff format --check` and `ruff check --no-fix` on tool_input.file_path only, returned as additionalContext; grandfather orchestrator.py via extend-per-file-ignores; auto-fix only on brand-new untracked files. (ruff format (write mode) reformats the entire file passed to it, not just changed lines; on a grandfathered legacy monolith this produces large noise diffs and breaks git blame / the pre-push hygiene hook. The fix (--check + --no-fix, surface as additionalContext, never auto-muta)

(Per-module ignore_errors=true is the documented per-file fence; follow_imports defaults to normal; mypy's own running-mypy guidance warns changed-files-only misses cross-file errors. MISSING: PROTECTED PATHS are the single biggest omission: .claude, .git, .mcp.json, .claude.json, .gitconfig, pre-commit/lefthook configs, .npmrc, .envrc, etc. are NEVER auto-approved by permissions.allow in default/acceptEdits/plan (prompted) and routed to the classifier in auto. This means (a) several proposed deny/ask rules on .claude/** are redundant with built-in behavior, and (b) any allow rule trying to auto-approve canon edits will silently fail. The bundle must be designed AROUND protected paths, not duplicate them. | No explicit guidance to put the run_tests.py wrapper behind async/asyncRewake. Running `.venv\Scripts\python.exe scripts\run_tests.py --stale-heartbeat=400` synchronously from a PostToolUse or Stop hook would freeze the session for minutes (a severe UX/autonomy regression). asyncRewake (exit 2 wakes Claude on failure) is the correct, documented pattern and is barely mentioned. | No mention of the official anthropics/claude-code examples/settings starter configs as the canonical baseline to diff against (the docs link a repo of starter settings). Building from those reduces hallucinated-key risk. | Hook PERFORMANCE/process-spawn budget on the 10,700-line orchestrator edit loop: matcher + the `if` field (fails open — performance filter only, never a security gate) and a single Node dispatcher to keep spawns to <=2/tool-call. The digest covers this but the final bundle must enforce it or every edit pays N cold-starts. | ConfigChange hook as a tamper-detector for prompt-injection that tries to widen permissions/remove hooks mid-session — advisory (exit 0 + additionalContext), never blocking (blocking ConfigChange would break the user's own routine canon maintenance and cannot block policy_settings anyway). | The lethal-trifecta framing for Ultron is mis-scoped: the real Ultron anticheat constraint (per the binding rules) is never default-loading the desktop/audio stack into RAM during a live game and using diagnostics testing mode — NOT blocking Claude's HTTPS doc fetches in a dev session. The bundle should not conflate the two; a network lockdown belongs in a live-game settings.local.json profile, not committed settings. | No validate_config.py / golden-digest / flavor-lint / test_anticheat integration plan: these existing deterministic gates should be invoked from the Stop/CI layer (scoped to changed files) rather than reinvented; the bundle should wire to them, not duplicate. | Secrets defense: a PreToolUse Write/Edit scan for inline-generated secrets (the only layer that catches secrets Claude WRITES, vs gitleaks which catches what's committed) — useful, but must updatedToolOutput/deny without false-blocking the legitimate corpus files that contain fake-key-shaped strings (allowlist needed). | No statement that defaultMode for Ultron/Kit should be 'default' (not auto/bypass) in committed project settings, and that auto belongs only in user-scope — the silently-ignored behavior means a project 'auto' is a no-op that gives false confidence. | Timeout pinning per hook (UserPromptSubmit defaults 30s and fires every prompt; command hooks default ~600s) — an unpinned slow hook can stall the whole session; the bundle must set explicit short timeouts on synchronous high-frequency hooks.
